1932.05.24

The Future of the New Japanese Cabinet

Since Prime Minister Inukai was assassinated, we have asserted that Japan would inevitably form a supra-party cabinet. Now, Saito has been appointed to succeed as the prime minister. The formation of a supra-party cabinet is a foregone conclusion. Our words have been verified. Because the situation has reached a point where there is no other way than to replace the political party cabinet with a supra-party cabinet.

After Inukai's assassination, the most talked-about figures to succeed him were Hiranuma, the leader of the Kokuhonsha, and Suzuki, the new president of the Seiyukai. However, it was difficult to predict who would ultimately win. When Saionji went to the capital to assess the situation, he felt compelled to follow the military's opinion and organize a supra-party cabinet, but he also dared not cause embarrassment to the political parties. He resolutely abandoned Hiranuma and Suzuki, who were at the center of the political storm. Saito was thus able to receive the imperial order. However, Saito, acting as a buffer, is gathering in the midst of the tide. It will be extremely difficult to cope with this difficult situation and win the favor of all parties. Therefore, the selection of cabinet members for the new cabinet was quite hesitant. It is natural that it was a difficult birth.

However, the establishment of the new cabinet will eventually become a reality within days. We don't need to spend time speculating. What we should pay attention to now is what its future will be after the new cabinet is produced, and what its impact on the world will be.

We believe that Saito's cabinet formation is more due to the victory of the military's advocacy than to Saionji's recommendation. We have said many times before that the Japanese fascist movement has reached its peak. The reason for the rise of fascist forces is actually due to the economic depression and the increasing severity of the recession, which stimulated the intensification of the left-leaning movement. Under this tide of economic panic, all social contradictions and crises are bound to erupt at any opportunity. The political party cabinet has no way to curb this crisis and stabilize politics, and the supra-party cabinet may not have this possibility. Even if a purely military cabinet is realized and fascism is vigorously implemented to suppress reaction, it will not be able to stop the tide of the times. Therefore, Saito's cabinet, under the impact of the current era, is only a bridge in a transitional era. We are very doubtful about whether its future will be bright and whether it will have a long and lasting political life.

After the establishment of the Saito Cabinet, it will definitely take the will of the military as its will. In other words, it will definitely vigorously implement militarism, intensify preparations for war against the United States and the Soviet Union externally, implement a tough policy toward us, and vigorously implement fascist politics internally to suppress the left-leaning movement, which will stimulate the increasing intensification of the left-leaning movement. The Osaka Asahi Shimbun published an article by Otake Hakuyoshi on the 13th, fearing that the Soviet Union would disrupt the situation in the event of a Japanese-American war and make Japan Sovietized. Therefore, he advocated easing relations with the Soviet Union. However, once a Japanese-American war breaks out, the world will immediately be engulfed in a vortex. Can Japan really avoid sudden changes during the war? In short, Japan's politics are now like a horse freed from its reins, galloping away and uncontrollable. Its future is certainly not optimistic.

Yesterday, Zhenru and Zhabei Were Taken Over

Today, Yanghang and Shizilin Will Be Taken Over

Tomorrow, Baoshan and Wusong Will Be Taken Over

Three hundred soldiers of the 1st Battalion, 9th Regiment, 9th Division of the Japanese Army in Zhenhua, completely withdrew at 11:00 a.m. yesterday. They were taken over by Shi Jinzhang, director of the 3rd Sub-District of the 4th District of our Municipal Public Security Bureau, and 72 police officers were dispatched to maintain order. The Japanese Naval Landing Forces in the jurisdiction of the 5th District, 2nd Sub-District, 4th District, etc., east of Zhongshan Road in Zhabei, west of Songhu Road, and north of Jinghu Road, also completely withdrew at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. Huang Ming, director of the Zhabei Office of the Public Security Bureau, took over. Local security was also maintained by plainclothes police officers on guard. Zhabei, which had been occupied for a long time, began to see the light of day again from yesterday afternoon. However, after the disaster, everything is waiting to be rebuilt, and it will take a long time to restore the original state. The details of the takeover are recorded below:

Zhenru Was Taken Over in the Morning

Departure of Takeover Personnel: Yesterday, the personnel who went to Zhenru to take over included: Tao Xiaojie, Liang Fuchu, and Cha Nanqiang from the committee; Gong Xikui, Shi Jinzhang, Yin Tixin, Cheng Jinxin, and Wu Qing from the Public Security Bureau; Hong Lanxiang, member of the municipal government; Ma Chonggan and Zhong Shijie from the Education Bureau; Sun Kairen and Zhuge Xun from the Public Works Bureau; Zhou Zanbang from the Public Works Bureau; Jiang Shicheng from the Health Bureau; Yu Ruilin, station manager of Zhenru Station; In addition, the Institute of Forensic Medicine, Jinan University, the Beijing-Hankou Power Line Bureau, the Telephone Bureau, and the China Business Electric Steam Company all sent personnel to participate in the takeover. At 8:00 a.m., they gathered at the Takeover Committee and departed for Zhenru together.

Arrangements Were Made Separately in Advance

Arriving in Zhenru at 8:30 a.m., they first went to the Japanese Army Headquarters at Xinmu Bridge to meet the captain, Inoue Sanichi. After the meeting, the Joint Committee, representatives from various countries, and Tao Xiaojie, the special envoy of the Takeover Committee, stayed at the headquarters for negotiations. The takeover personnel from various agencies rushed to the Municipal Committee of Zhenshang to rest temporarily and arrange their positions and the steps of the takeover. Then, the Japanese side sent Deputy Adjutant Yamakawa Yoshiharu to inform our takeover personnel that they could first go to various places to make preliminary arrangements. So, twenty police officers were dispatched to advance to the vicinity of Xinmu Bridge at 9:40 a.m., and after the Japanese army withdrew, they would be deployed in the town. The remaining personnel from various agencies also went to make arrangements.

Formal Handover Procedures

Then, at around 10:00 a.m., the handover procedures began. At that time, in addition to our takeover personnel and representatives from various countries, the Japanese side included Captain Inoue Sanichi, Deputy Adjutant Yamakawa Yoshiharu, and translator Kojima Seiichi. First, British Military Officer Brand showed the map, and Director Wen Yingsing and Japanese Military Officer Harada checked it. Then, the handover document was issued, and the handover personnel from both sides signed it. Our side was Shi Jinzhang, Director of the 3rd Sub-District of the 4th District, and the Japanese side was Captain Inoue Sanichi.

Exchange of Documents Between China and Japan

Yesterday, the exchange of documents between China and Japan was completely different from the withdrawal of Japanese troops in other areas. The original text of the exchange of documents between China and Japan is recorded below. The original Japanese text reads: (1) All the houses and furniture used by the Japanese army have been completely handed over without any remainder. (2) At 11:00 a.m. on May 22, Showa 7, the security of Zhenru and the Zhenru Town and Zhenru Station area has indeed been handed over to your side. (3) We are not responsible for any accidents that occur after the withdrawal of the Japanese army. May 23, Showa 7, Inoue Sanichi, Captain of the Zhenru District Garrison, Infantry Major. Our original text reads: (1) The houses near Zhenru Town and Zhenru Railway Station where the Japanese army was stationed and the furniture in the houses have been accurately received without error. (2) At 11:00 a.m. on May 23, Showa 7, the security of Zhenru Town and Zhenru Railway Station area was indeed taken over by the Japanese army. (3) From now on, the security of this place will be maintained by our side. It goes without saying that the responsibility for any accidents that occur after the withdrawal of the Japanese army does not lie with our army. May 23, 21st year of the Republic of China, Shi Jinzhang, Zhenru Takeover Commissioner, Director of the 3rd Sub-District of the 4th District of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau. (Reporter's note: The above exchange of documents was drafted by the Japanese side in advance.)

The Beiping Security Team Arrived

The seventy-two members of the Beiping Security Team who opened to Zhenru yesterday were originally stationed on Menggu Road in Zhabei. Yesterday, due to the takeover of Zhenru, they were led by Chief Instructor Ma Hongru and Patrol Officer Zhang Shengfu of the 3rd Sub-District of the 4th District, and departed from Zhabei at 9:00 a.m., passing through Caojiadu, Zhongshan Road, and arriving in Zhenru. It was 10:00 a.m. Then, they were notified by Hong Lanxiang, Tao Xiaojie, etc. to go to the town to set up posts. Another twenty people were deployed in the vicinity of Jinghu Road. However, from today onwards, the security of Zhenru will still be maintained by the police of the 3rd Sub-District of the 4th District. The Beiping Security Team will be transferred back to Zhabei.

The Situation of the Japanese Army's Withdrawal

The three hundred soldiers of the 1st Battalion of the 9th Division finally left in the Zhenru area. Except for the fifteen people stationed at No. 47 South Main Street in the town, the rest were stationed near Zhenru Station. The Japanese army south of the railway completed the preparation of guns and horses at around 9:00 a.m. The baggage and food were first transported back to the town by more than ten trucks. The fifteen people moved to Jinan training ground at 9:40 a.m. The soldiers and sentries stationed in other houses also gathered at Jinan training ground one after another at 10:20 a.m. At 10:30 a.m., Inoue gave a speech and reviewed the troops at the field for half an hour. At 11:05 a.m., they marched in formation towards Zhongxing Road and withdrew.

Post-War Matters in Zhenru

During the battle, Zhenru Town was in the rear, so the destruction of houses was not very serious. However, after the Japanese army entered, the loss of residents' property was very great. Just the residence of Mr. Chen Depei, occupied by the 1st Battalion of the Japanese Army, the antiques and ancient paintings were all taken away, and the loss reached more than 9,000 yuan. The rest can be imagined. In addition, the school supplies and furniture of Jinan University were looted by the Japanese army, and a part of them was seized by the maintenance association of the puppet organization. Yesterday, the representative of the school, Yang Yufen, asked Shi Jinzhang, the director of the 3rd Sub-District of the 4th District, to conduct a thorough investigation of each household to return a part of it. As for Shen Songge, the so-called chairman of the Zhenru Local Maintenance Association of the puppet organization, he has disappeared yesterday.

Zhabei Was Taken Over in the Afternoon Takeover Procedures in Zhabei

At 2:30 p.m. yesterday, our takeover personnel officially took over the area north of the Zhabei Railway. The handover ceremony was held at the headquarters of the 3rd Battalion of the Japanese Army in Anhui Middle School on Zhongxing Road. The Japanese Navy authorities also stipulated the following procedures for the second takeover of Zhabei: (1) Chinese Committee members in attendance, (2) Japanese Committee members seated, (3) Handshake between Commander Mori and Commander Huang Ming, (4) Commander Mori's handover

The Situation of the Beiping Security Team Arriving in Zhabei (Photo by Xu Tianzhang)

Declaration (translation), signature (5) Commander Huang Ming's general declaration (translation), signature (6) Handshake between the two

Departure of Takeover Personnel

The Takeover Committee appointed special envoys Cha Nanqiang, Tao Xiaojie, and Li Shengjun to be responsible for the handover. After completing the handover in Zhenru at 11:30 a.m. yesterday, the special envoys went directly to Zhabei to negotiate the handover with the Japanese side. Huang Ming, Long Xikui, Yin Tixin, He Yiming, and Niu Jingjian from the Public Security Bureau; Gu Xianbai from the Public Works Bureau; Zhong Shijie from the Education Bureau; He Bingsong from the Commercial Press; and Zeng Zhihong from the Two-Road Bureau gathered at Jiangping Nursery on Yuyingtang Road at 1:30 p.m. At 1:40 p.m., they departed together to the headquarters of the 2nd Battalion of the Japanese Navy to hold the takeover ceremony.

The Situation of the Handover Between the Two Sides

At 1:45 p.m., the committee members from China, Britain, the United States, Italy, and other countries of the Joint Committee came to the headquarters of the 3rd Battalion of the Japanese Navy in Anhui Middle School to monitor the withdrawal of the Japanese army. After the committee members of the Joint Committee arrived at the scene, they successively studied the map and carefully verified the withdrawal points of the Japanese army. At that time, the Japanese army was gathered in the courtyard of Anhui Middle School. At 2:10 p.m., the handover ceremony was held. Mori Kakuyoshi, Commander of the 1st Battalion of the Japanese Navy, and Huang Ming, Commander of our Police Battalion, took their positions. First, Japanese Commander Mori Kakuyoshi gave a speech, saying that China and Japan were unfortunately enemies, and today, a truce and troop withdrawal have been realized and a satisfactory solution has been reached, which he feels very happy about. In this war, both China and Japan sacrificed many precious lives, which he feels very painful about. Looking back on the past, he feels even more regret. Since the Japanese Navy entered Zhabei, there have been few Japanese residents in Zhabei and many Chinese residents. However, the Japanese army has prevented security and treated everyone equally, so that the people can live and work in peace. Fortunately, there has been nothing wrong for more than a month. Now that local security is handed over to the Chinese side, he hopes that the Chinese police can maintain security as usual, restore order, and do their best to protect Japanese residents, so that Zhabei, where the Japanese army has been stationed, will become a model area in Shanghai in the future, which he hopes for. After Commander Nichida finished speaking, Commander Huang Ming of our side gave a speech, saying that in this Sino-Japanese war, the two countries were unhappy. Now that a truce and troop withdrawal have been achieved, he will protect the local area as much as possible, regardless of class or nationality, and do his best to maintain it. After the speech, Commander Nichida and Commander Huang Ming shook hands and decided to carry out the document exchange procedures.

The Original Text of the Handover Document

(1) No abnormality in the security maintenance and guard area, (2) (Area) West of Hongkou, north of Huning Railway, south of Yinying Road, (3) (Occupied buildings) The occupied state is preserved, middle school (that is, Anhui Middle School) Jinglu Temple, (4) (Occupied movable property) Separate line pass (that is, the meaning of another attached book) (5) (Criminals) None

The Japanese Army Retreated in Formation

The Japanese Navy stationed in Zhabei has a total of 13 two battalions. The commander of the first battalion is Mori Kakukyu, and the commander of the third battalion is Oeyan. Yesterday, after the document exchange procedures were completed, at 2:30 p.m., all the Japanese troops began to withdraw, walking east along Zhongxing Road to Zhongxing Road to gather with the first battalion, and then walking east along Dongxing Road to Jiangwan Road into the Hongkou Japanese area. The Japanese troops were well-equipped, and there were two armored vehicles to protect the rear when they withdrew.

Pingjing Takes Over Zhabei

Yesterday, the two battalions of Pingjing, totaling more than 200, were responsible for taking over Zhabei. At 1:40 p.m., they were stationed at Jiangping Nursery on Gonghe Xin Road and Yuyingtang Road. After the Japanese army withdrew, the police team was stationed in each area to take over. Yesterday, when the Pingjing went to take over the defense, the chief commander Lu Lu also went to arrange it. The area was originally under the jurisdiction of the 5th District General Office and the 2nd Sub-District of the 5th District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. From yesterday, it has resumed office. The 5th District General Office is temporarily located at Shen's residence, No. 537 Hongxing Road, the headquarters address of the army's first battalion. The 2nd Office of the 5th District is temporarily stationed at Jiangping Nursery on Yuyingtang Road.

Joint Committee Inspects

The Joint Committee, Sang Hai'er, Brand, Faratini, Wen Yingsing, Harada Kumakichi, etc., after the takeover was completed, took cars to inspect the junction where the Japanese army temporarily stationed after the withdrawal of the Japanese army from Yokohama River. They were afraid that the Japanese army and our police would misunderstand each other across the river in the future, and inspected the post-war situation there. A group of six people exited Anhui Middle School, entered Gonghe Xin Road, Hutai Road, Zhongshan Road, Sanyang Road, Gujiawan, and Yokohama River along Zhongxing Road, a distance of more than a hundred weapons, that is, the Eight Character Bridge, which was the most intense place recorded in the war where the two armies faced each other for more than a month. There were almost no complete houses within dozens of miles around. Along the way, broken walls, rubble, scorched earth, and debris were piled up like mounds. The factory buildings, chimneys, etc. that had not been bombed or burned out were also mostly penetrated by cannonballs, like opening doors and households, and the holes in the bullets were even denser than beehives. After inspecting, the committee members went to the nearby Japanese crematorium and cemetery to inspect, and then took the cars and turned back, crossing the Songhu Railway from Xinmin Road, Tongji Road, and Jiangwan Road, and entered the concession from North Sichuan Road and dispersed.

Taking Over Zhenru and Zhabei Schools

Yesterday morning, the Zhenru area was taken over, including Jinan University, Southeast Medical College, and nine municipal primary schools, including Zhenru, Guanlong, Pengcheng, Gucun, Changtou, Xincun, Yanlong, Luku, and Ganlu. In the afternoon, the Zhabei area was taken over, including 26 private schools, such as Shibei, and 6 municipal primary schools, such as Peiben. The Municipal Education Bureau sent Ma Chonggan, Zhong Shijie, Zhang Yanggao, Zhou Shang, Zhu Chenggui, Li Haihong, Zhang Meisun, Yao Changjiong, etc., accompanied by the responsible personnel of each school, to take over and inspect. It was found that Guangdong, Shanggong, Shibei, Daozhong, Yude, Huifeng, Jiancheng, Xinming, Jianguo, Zhabei Kindergarten, Peiben, and other 26 schools in Zhabei were completely burned down on the fire line. China Women's Physical School and Pengnan Primary School only had empty school buildings left, and the items were looted. The losses in Zhenru schools were relatively small. Jinan and Southeast Medical College were bombed in many places, and the school equipment was lost, resulting in huge losses.

Yanghang and Shizilin Will Be Taken Over Today

The Japanese troops in the north of Zhenru and Zhabei withdrew separately yesterday morning and afternoon, and were taken over by our side. The Japanese troops in Yanghang and Shizilin Fortress will also withdraw at the same time at 11:00 a.m. this morning. A squadron of the Capital Security Team, which was taken over by our side, has been transferred to Yuepu by Captain Bian, and will go to take over at 11:00 a.m. today, together with Wang Qingtao, the district chief of the first district of Baoshan County, and Shi Ze, the takeover commissioner of the takeover committee.

Baoshan and Wusong Will Be Taken Over Tomorrow Departing for Inspection Today

The Japanese troops in Baoshan and Wusong have decided to withdraw tomorrow. The Takeover Committee decided to send personnel to inspect and negotiate the takeover of Wusong, and designated Yin Tixin, Li Jing, Tao Xiaojie, and Tang Chengzong to negotiate everything with the Japanese side. They will gather at the association at 7:10 a.m. this morning and must depart at 8:00 a.m.

Police Dispatched to Handle the Takeover

The Takeover Committee also ordered Sun Xiwu, the county magistrate of Baoshan County, to order 30 to 50 provincial police officers to arrive outside Baoshan City before 9:00 a.m. tomorrow to handle the takeover with the Capital Security Team.

Jiangwan Police Replaced

The Takeover Committee also ordered Bian Zhishan, the commander of the Capital Security Team, to order a squadron of police officers currently stationed in Jiangwan to arrive outside Baoshan County before 9:00 a.m. tomorrow to handle the takeover with Sun Xiwu, the county magistrate of Baoshan County. The defense of Jiangwan Town will be handed over to Dai Hongen, the director of the 5th Sub-District of the 5th District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who will lead the Beiping Security Team to take over.

The Current Situation of Pengpu After the Takeover

Since Pengpu Town was taken over by our side on the 19th of this month, there has been a squad of the Capital Security Police, totaling more than 30 people, stationed there. The leaders of the defense regiment, Hou Qizhang, Zhou Buli, Shangguan Rong, Zhao Zuyan, and Wang Yingxiang, personally lead their departments to patrol day and night. Therefore, the town and its vicinity have been peaceful as usual in recent days. The reporter of Xinsheng News Agency met Ling Zhibin, the municipal committee member of the district yesterday, who said that the municipal office of the district has been operating as usual since the 19th, and Pengpu Primary School also started classes on the 20th. In terms of transportation, since Zhabei has been taken over by our side, there have been no traces of the Japanese army between Shanghai and Pengpu since yesterday afternoon. Yu (Ling Jun himself) personally visited the entire area between 5:00 and 6:00 p.m. today (the 23rd), east to Yemaowan, north to Dachang Town, west to Dayang Bridge and Wangjiajing, and south to Zhongbei Road, Qiujiang Road, Yongxing Road, and Zhijiangmiao Road, transportation is convenient, and there are police posts everywhere. The new Yingpan branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau also resumed operation at 4:00 p.m. today, and Chen Xuemin is still the patrol officer. The 2nd team of the Zhongxing Road Pengpu Defense Regiment also resumed posting at 3:00 p.m. today. Most of the shops in the district have also opened for business. Therefore, please ask your reporter to publish the peaceful situation in detail, hoping that the people who have not returned to their hometown will move back immediately. The reporter also asked about the serious disaster situation in your district as reported in the newspapers, and how to provide relief in the future. He replied that the houses in the district, such as Yongxing Road and Qiujiang Road, were all burned down. The relief method here is planned to be handled in the same way as in Zhabei. As for the rural farm households, in addition to distributing tens of thousands of pounds of cotton seeds three weeks ago, they are now contacting the four districts of Wusong, Jiangwan, Yinhang, and Zhenru to prepare a relief plan, such as providing loans, clothing, medical treatment, disaster relief, and organizing small industries, and jointly submitting it to the Municipal Government for separate implementation.

The Status of the Postal Workers' Strike on the Second Day

Airmail Efforts to Deliver

Preparing for an International Temporary Post Office

Huang Naishu Took Office Yesterday

The General Labor Union is Conducting Mediation

The general strike of postal workers in the city entered its second day yesterday. Although Mayor Wu and others made every effort to mediate, there was no progress. In order to rescue international postal delivery, the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession consulted with the municipal government and the French Concession authorities yesterday morning to discuss countermeasures, and decided to set up a temporary post office to send and receive international mail. Huang Naishu, the new director of the Post Office, took office yesterday morning. Details are recorded as follows:

Airmail Delivery as Usual

Since China Aviation Corporation announced that it would continue to collect and deliver airmail as usual, the number of people who came to the company to send airmail yesterday was very crowded, and the company's staff also worked overtime due to the work of checking and sorting letters. In order to protect the safety of the staff, the company has negotiated with the police station to send more police officers to the office for protection. The Longhua Aircraft Factory has also dispatched 40 police and security team members from the Public Security Bureau to protect it permanently. All the airmail from various places that arrived in Shanghai the day before was also delivered by dozens of Boy Scouts hired by the company. Yesterday afternoon, all of them were delivered. When the Boy Scouts were delivering letters, the company also asked the police station and the Public Security Bureau to order the police officers on duty to pay attention to protection. Therefore, the Boy Scouts' service was very safe. The recipients and the public were grateful and admired the energetic Boy Scouts who were delivering letters.

Opening a Temporary Post Office

The Public Works Bureau decided to open a temporary emergency post office dedicated to receiving and sending international mail due to the strike at the Shanghai Post Office. It will begin operations at 9:30 a.m. this morning. The address is located on the third floor of the Public Works Bureau on Fuzhou Road. Feeson, Director of the Public Works Bureau, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Merihac, French Consul-General, and Zaplin, Director of the Shanghai Post Office, met at the Public Works Bureau at 11:00 a.m. yesterday morning to discuss the matter and decided to handle it. At the beginning of the opening, only letters to Hong Kong and foreign countries will be accepted. The method of postage is to issue a kind of letter coupon, each five coupons are sold for one yuan, and each letter is affixed with one coupon. If you want to register, you need to add two more letter coupons. The Public Works Bureau has now assigned a number of temporary staff, but it is afraid that it will not be enough, and it is still recruiting volunteers to serve as letter pickers or other positions. If you have anything to contact with this post office, you can write to Mr. Lan, the director of the Public Works Bureau. This post office is completely temporary and emergency in nature, because the work of the Chinese Post Office is currently suspended.

Foreign Ships Allowed to Collect and Send

The Great American Evening Post said that the reporter of this newspaper inquired about various shipping companies this (23rd) morning, and most of them are also willing to receive letters and postcards to facilitate the public. However, registered letters are not accepted. All letters with sufficient postage affixed by the sender can be received by Changxing Dalai Consulting Company and sent to various export ships. And various wheel bill rooms can also receive this kind of letter and sell stamps. The companies such as Beide and Henry are not convenient to receive mail in the company, only the ships can receive it, but they must affix sufficient German postage. The Japan Mail Ship Company can also receive letters with sufficient Chinese postage affixed, and its ships can also receive letters.

Accommodation Measures for Deposit Withdrawals

After the postal workers' strike, regarding postal savings and remittances, in addition to the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau at No. 5 Fuzhou Road and the National Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, which continue to operate as usual, the remaining branches are closed because they have always been handled by postal workers. Yesterday, the reporter visited the manager of the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. According to the manager, after the postal workers' strike, the savings and remittance branches in this port were temporarily suspended because they were previously handled by the post office. Now, the branch deposit households have decided on the following accommodation measures: (1) The branch deposit households who have a passbook for accommodation savings can withdraw deposits from the head office at No. 5 Fuzhou Road. (2) Non-accommodation savings in each branch, because the head office does not have the seal of the deposit household, are difficult to handle and must be temporarily suspended. In case the strike extends gradually, a new method will be found to accommodate non-accommodation savings. As for the staff in the head office who joined the postal workers' union, there are only fifteen people, although they are also on strike, but it has no impact.

Huang Nai-shu Assumes Office Yesterday

The Ministry of Transportation, suspecting Qian Chunqi, the Director-General of the Postal Administration, of inciting the recent postal workers' strike, detained him in the capital a few days ago. He is currently being held at the Garrison Headquarters. Huang Nai-shu has been appointed to replace him as Director-General of the Postal Administration. After receiving the appointment, Mr. Huang arrived at the office yesterday morning (the 23rd) at 10 a.m. to take charge. Lin Shi, the representative of the Ministry of Transportation, delivered a speech. Those who attended the inauguration ceremony yesterday included Lin Shi, the representative of the Ministry of Transportation, Zhong Shigang, the Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Transportation, Yang Jianping, the Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, Liu Peiquan, the General Manager of China National Aviation Corporation, and over fifty staff members of the Postal Administration. At 10:20 a.m., Mr. Huang arrived with officials from the Ministry of Transportation, and the inauguration ceremony immediately began. Lin Shi delivered a speech, followed by a speech by Yang Jianping. Finally, Mr. Huang gave a response. After the ceremony, everyone dispersed.

Expression of the Strike Committee

The Strike Committee sent representatives Zhang Kechang, Qi Jiamou, Chuan Dewei, and Shi Yitang, among others, to meet with Mayor Wu at the City Hall on the afternoon before last. After the meeting, they reported the details back to the Strike Committee. The committee, after hearing the report, immediately convened a plenary meeting and seriously considered the situation. They believe that the proposed plan to consolidate the postal foundation is of great importance to the future of the postal service, so they are willing to take the final action to achieve it. During this critical period, they sincerely hope that the Ministry of Transportation will openly accept the proposal so that it can be resolved as soon as possible. They also sent a letter to various sectors of society, which stated: "Dear Sirs, Our committee, in view of the repeated requests to implement the plan to consolidate the

Page 4

postal foundation, which have been rejected by the Ministry of Transportation, and the instability of the postal service, which is as precarious as a pile of eggs, cannot bear to sit idly by and watch the collapse of the postal service. We have no choice but to endure hardship and pain and rise up to save ourselves. We have declared a strike from the 22nd of this month in the hope that the transportation authorities will awaken. Our committee is in a state of great distress. Now, we sincerely inform all sectors of society that this strike is truly out of love for the postal service and to save it. Our loyalty and sincerity can be testified by Heaven and Earth. Considering that the postal service is a public utility and is closely related to all sectors of society, we hope that you will sympathize with our efforts to save the postal service. We have always admired your leadership and your upholding of righteousness. We earnestly request your assistance to maintain the postal service. We offer our most sincere prayers."

The Rise of Supporters

The entire staff of the Supply Division of the Jiaozhou Road Postal Administration, numbering over two hundred, are also members of the two associations and have now joined in the unified action. It is understood that the Supply Division is the central hub for the supply of postal supplies and stationery nationwide. In addition, those who have offered assistance and condolences include: (1) The Tongyi Association of clerks of the Shanghai Wireless Telegraph Main Station of the Ministry of Transportation sent a letter to the association, which stated: "Dear Sirs, Your association's contribution of grand ideas for striving for the consolidation of the state-owned transportation industry and seeking ways to save the postal service has been rejected by the authorities. You have not avoided difficulties and have resolutely persevered in your struggle. We express our utmost admiration and sympathy. Our association, on behalf of all its members, extends our sincere wishes that your association will achieve final victory and reach its initial goals. We will do our best within our capabilities to provide assistance. This letter is sent to express our condolences and to seek your understanding." (2) The Shanghai Toothbrush Industry Union, the Shanghai Ink Manufacturing Industry Union, and others have also sent letters of condolence. In addition, the employees of the five wharves of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Shanghai-Ningbo Steamboat Tea Room, the Steamboat Wood Industry, the Ink Manufacturing, the Hat Manufacturing, the Cigarette Rolling in the four districts, the Knitting in the two districts, the Shipbuilding in the one district, the Laundry, the Dyeing in the three districts, the Shipbuilding in the four districts, the Cleaning in the four districts, the Public Transportation in the six districts, the Lithography, the Tobacco Exchange, the Sauce Industry, the Pharmaceutical Industry, the Tea and Snack Industry, the Water and Electricity in the six districts, the Toothbrush Industry, the Cotton Spinning in the seven districts, the Fragrance Industry, the Dyeing Industry, the Silk Weaving and Garment Making in the two districts, the Rubber Industry in the six districts, the Soap and Medicine in the nine districts, the Egg Industry in the four districts, the Sand Casting, the Catering, and the Inland Steamboat and more than seventy other labor unions also jointly issued a declaration yesterday in support.

The Mediation of the General Labor Union

The Shanghai General Labor Union, in response to the postal strike, convened a temporary emergency meeting yesterday morning at 10 a.m., chaired by Zhou Xuexiang. The following measures were decided to provide assistance: (1) Telegraph the Executive Yuan to promptly adopt the plan so that it can be resolved as soon as possible. (2) Issue a declaration. (3) Issue a letter to fellow workers. (4) Appoint Li Yongxiang, Zhou Xuexiang, Yu Xianting, Shao Xubai, Lu Muqin, Weng Ruifu, Long Peiyun, and Liu Jintai to consult with the municipal government on mediation opinions. (5) Schedule a representative assembly to discuss further measures. (6) Appoint Zhou Xuexiang, Weng Ruifu, Yu Xianting, and Li Yongxiang to offer condolences. Yesterday afternoon at 3 p.m., Li Yongxiang and others went to the City Hall to inquire about the mayor's mediation opinions. Because the mayor was attending a takeover meeting, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun met with them on his behalf. The two sides exchanged opinions. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun hoped that the General Labor Union should sympathize with the postal strike but should also consider the government's position and do its best to persuade the workers not to expand the labor unrest. He also promised to convey the representatives' opinions to the mayor and schedule another meeting to discuss the matter. The telegraph sent by the union to the Executive Yuan is as follows: "To President Wang of the Executive Yuan, Nanjing: The Shanghai postal workers, in order to save the postal service from its perilous state, have carefully considered the matter and pledged their loyalty. They have submitted a plan to consolidate the postal foundation to the Ministry of Transportation. The various points they have raised are in fact the unanimous demands of all sectors of society. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Citizens' Federation, and other organizations have all sympathized and responded. However, the Ministry of Transportation has not only failed to adopt the plan but has also accused them of deliberately causing trouble and has slandered them. As a result, the postal workers' emotions have boiled over, leading to this unfortunate strike. The Ministry of Transportation cannot escape blame for its improper handling of the situation. Now that the strike has already broken out, if it is not properly handled, there is a risk of it spreading across the country. The impact would be extremely significant. Therefore, we urgently request the Executive Yuan to promptly instruct the Ministry of Transportation to comply with public opinion and adopt the plan as much as possible so that it can be resolved as soon as possible and avoid expanding the unrest. We are extremely anxious. We respectfully send this telegraph and request your consideration and implementation. Shanghai General Labor Union."

Investigation of Bribery and Transportation Preparation

According to responsible representatives of the two postal unions, since the news was reported the day before yesterday that the Ministry of Transportation had received a secret report that someone had used 30,000 yuan to instigate the Shanghai postal workers' strike, the two unions believe that this movement is entirely for the love of the postal service and to save it. The intention is extremely clear. This kind of secret report affects the reputation of the two unions and is infuriating. The two unions immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Transportation to thoroughly investigate the truth and make a clear statement. To this day, the Ministry of Transportation has not made a clear statement as to whether the news reported is accurate. The two unions have now entrusted their legal counsel, lawyers Jiang Yiping and Chen Tingrui, to prepare the procedures to file a public lawsuit in accordance with the law to protect their reputation and legal rights.

Clarification of the Ministry of Transportation's Clarification

The Strike Committee of the Shanghai Postal Workers Union and the Shanghai Postal Employees Union believes that there are many errors in the points made by the Ministry of Transportation in its clarification of the two unions' proposed plan to consolidate the postal foundation, which were published in today's newspapers. Therefore, they are providing further clarification based on the facts, which states: "Upon investigation, the Ministry of Transportation's arguments can be summarized into five points: (1) Copying Japanese precedents necessitates separation. (2) Developing postal savings and remittances requires a separate bureau. (3) Selecting specialized talent for the Savings and Remittance Bureau does not require examination, and the Postal Administration does not need to be involved. Regarding the other points, the facts about the dismissal of the former director and the appointment of personnel within the bureau, as well as the recall of postal personnel, are self-evident and do not require clarification from our committee. Let us first discuss the Japanese precedents. Japan is a small country, but because its national economy is prosperous, its total savings exceed 300 million yuan. Therefore, it is necessary to have separate bureaus to manage it. China's postal lines are extensive, and its postal districts are vast, but its total savings are only 30 million yuan. The size of the business scope differs by a hundredfold. It is like a poor family pretending to be wealthy, which is ridiculous. Moreover, the management rights of the Japanese Savings Bureau still remain within the postal system. The administrative and personnel systems are also the same as the postal system. Although they are separated, they are not truly separated. The establishment of another bureau is only another part of the Postal Administration. It is not like our Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, where the Postal Administration does not need to be involved. Since it is called the postal service, how can the Postal Administration not need to be involved? What is the meaning of the word 'General' in the name 'Postal Administration'? The bureau also operates banking business, which is not allowed by national laws and is also not permitted by the Japanese Savings Bureau. As for the speculative, extravagant, and various other businesses that should not and cannot be carried out in the postal service, the bureau engages in them all, thinking it is a proud creation, but it does not know that it is greatly contrary to the original purpose of establishing postal savings. The so-called imitation of Japanese precedents is neither in name nor in substance, and it is truly a mere imitation with no value. This is the first point. The Ministry of Transportation says that postal savings were not developed under the management of the Postal Administration, so there is a need to set up a specialized management organization and vigorously promote it. This shows a lack of understanding of the internal affairs of the postal service and the function of savings. The postal service is a state-owned enterprise whose purpose is to facilitate the public. Its operation of postal savings is to encourage limited savings by ordinary people. It is not comparable to ordinary banking businesses. Therefore, the Postal Administration has restrictions on the operation of savings. Individual savings cannot exceed 2,000 yuan per year, and group savings cannot exceed 3,000 yuan per year. Monthly savings cannot exceed 200 yuan. These regulations show that the reason why rural savings could not increase in the past was due to the postal service's business policy. It was not a question of setting up a bureau to manage and promote it. If the postal bureau cancels the restriction policy and operates according to the methods of banks, then the amount of increase may be more than what it is now. Moreover, given the current state of poverty among the people, ordinary people do not even have enough to eat and wear, so they have no surplus to save. It is difficult for postal savings to achieve a sudden increase. This is the result of social change. To think that setting up another bureau and promoting it can promote its development is truly ignorant of the content of postal savings and the national and social conditions, and it is a Utopian dream. Let us also discuss the item of remittances. Before the separation, the total amount of remittances reached more than 130 million yuan per year. According to the statistics for last year, it only reached more than 160 million yuan. The so-called promotion and development is indeed the case. Why does the Ministry of Transportation deliberately exaggerate its claims and deceive society? This is the second point. The Ministry of Transportation says that the personnel of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau are experts and are also postal workers. Why should there be such a clear distinction and opposition? I do not know that what our committee opposes is the system, not the people. The postal service has many businesses, and there are quite a few talents. The selection and appointment of personnel is not like the rapid turnover of the bureau. It is based on formal examinations by the postal bureau. During the term of appointment, promotion, demotion, rewards, and punishments all have a fixed system. There has never been the arbitrary appointment and dismissal of personnel like in the bureau. The postal examination system is a common practice for the appointment of personnel in various civilized countries. It is not a matter of taking an examination to monopolize the business. As for the Ministry of Transportation's saying that postal personnel cannot be proficient in savings and remittance business, and the necessity of selecting experts, let us ask, postal savings have been managed by postal personnel for thirty years, and the main directors and section chiefs of the bureau must be transferred from postal personnel. The business in various places must also be handled by postal personnel. Why deny the facts and say that there are no talents who are proficient in savings and remittance among postal personnel? Moreover, the experts selected by the bureau are either relatives of powerful people or are supported by friends. In fact, they all hold ordinary clerical positions. The daily documents and official duties are not entirely related to savings and remittance. This shows that their words are unfounded. This is the third point. As for the Ministry of Transportation's saying that setting up a separate bureau does not waste postal funds, it is a blatant lie. After the establishment of the bureau, because it is another main bureau, it must pay 360,000 yuan per year to the Ministry of Transportation for routine expenses, according to the example of the Postal Administration. The bureau's headquarters and the two branch bureaus in Hankou and Nanjing have deputy directors, directors, deputy directors, managers, deputy managers, section chiefs, section members, clerks, trainees, police officers, consultants, and committee members, etc. The salaries and office expenses amount to 1.56 million yuan, which are all borne by the postal bureau. The branch expenses of the National Bureau for the combined operation of savings and remittance business are more than 6 million yuan. The so-called no waste of funds is shocking. In short, the bureau has been separated for three years, and the results have been shown to society through the recent increase in postal rates. If the Ministry of Transportation does not promptly pull back from the brink and merge the bureau back into the Postal Administration, then the postal foundation will be shaken, and the result of the postal service will be no different from that of the telegraph and navigation. The two associations base their sincere suggestions to the Ministry of Transportation on their experience in serving the postal service. Sending telegrams and petitions is time-consuming and laborious, which is unbearable. What they care about is protecting the last remaining postal service in the country, preserving the interests of the people and the dignity of the country. The Ministry of Transportation is the national transportation administrative agency, and it should openly accept the will of the people. The people's suggestions for improving the business are by no means comparable to coercion or interference in administration. It is the expression of the spirit of democracy. Moreover, the postal foundation is being shaken and urgently needs to be rescued."

Wang Jingwei's Instruction

A Central News Agency report from Nanjing on the 23rd stated: "President Wang of the Executive Yuan telegraphed Mayor Wu of Shanghai on the 23rd, saying: 'To Mayor Wu Tiecheng of Shanghai, Today's political meeting has decided on the policy regarding the postal workers' strike. The Executive Yuan is instructing the Shanghai Municipal Government as follows: According to your telegram of the 22nd, the Shanghai Postal Employees Union and the Postal Workers Union held a strike at 5 a.m. today. Article 3 of the Trade Union Law states that employees and workers of national administrative, transportation, military, and state-owned industries shall not invoke this law to organize trade unions. Article 23 also states that trade unions organized by workers in the industries listed in Article 3 shall not declare strikes. Article 37 states that when a trade union has any of the following circumstances, the competent authorities shall disband it: (1) The basic elements of existence are not available; (2) The violation of laws and regulations is serious; (3) The disruption of public order or harm to the public interest. Now, the Shanghai postal workers are not abiding by the laws and regulations and are holding a strike at a time when the situation is serious and the country is in difficulty, which is a form of coercion. This has a significant impact on the country and society. The government should immediately instruct the competent authorities to handle it in accordance with the law. Now, we are giving leniency and instructing you, Mayor, to earnestly persuade the postal workers to return to work immediately. The government will consider whether or not to handle the suggestions regarding postal affairs separately. If they still do not realize their mistake, then the government, in order to protect the national transportation agencies, public order, and the public interest, will have to implement strict measures. This is the instruction. You must comply and not disobey. This order is from Wang Zhaoming, President of the Executive Yuan."

Chen Mingshu's Statement

A special dispatch from Nanjing on the 23rd stated: "Chen Mingshu told the press on the 23rd regarding the Shanghai postal unrest that the Shanghai postal strike had been brewing for a long time, and the government had made considerable preparations and would thoroughly resolve it soon without expanding the unrest. The reasons for the strike put forward by the trade unions are not related to the interests of the postal workers themselves but involve the national administrative system, which is very unconventional. Within my authority, in addition to reporting to the central government for thorough handling in accordance with the law, there is no other way. According to reports, the striking workers posted many improper slogans, such as 'Down with so-and-so' and 'Support so-and-so.' These troublemakers are not to be pitied, but it is a great pity that the majority of postal workers who have been loyal to their duties and have contributed to the national revolution are also affected by the minority."

Yu Feipeng's Report

A special dispatch from Nanjing on the 23rd stated: "Transportation Vice Minister Yu Feipeng reported at the memorial week on the 33rd that he believed that the four demands of the Shanghai postal union were unreasonable. He also said that Minister Chen dismissed Long Dafu, the Director of the Postal Affairs Department, because he did not handle the unrest well. It is the inherent right of the superior to discipline the subordinate for dereliction of duty. Director Qian Chunqi was detained because of reports from various sources that Qian was suspected of being involved in the strike. He has now been handed over to the judicial authorities for handling."

A Reuters dispatch from Nanjing on the 23rd stated: "Transportation Vice Minister Yu Feipeng announced at a ministry meeting today that the Ministry of Transportation has agreed to restore the rice allowance for postal employees with monthly salaries below 80 yuan. The plan to cut staff and reduce administration will also be postponed. However, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau cannot be merged with the Postal Administration as requested by the strikers. In addition, the contracts signed with various airlines cannot be canceled."

Chen Gongbo Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

A Reuters dispatch from Nanjing on the 33rd stated: "The government is paying close attention to the postal workers' strike in Shanghai. Yesterday, the leaders held a full-day meeting in Tangshan to discuss mediation methods. Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo has been ordered by President Wang to travel to Shanghai this morning to investigate the truth."

Lin Shi Denies Mediation

According to sources from the central government yesterday, the rumor that the Ministry of Transportation had sent former Postal Administrator Lin Shi to mediate the postal unrest is not true. As for the case of Mr. Lin's contract for printing stamps during his tenure as administrator, the central government had investigated and found no evidence of corruption. The 9th State Council meeting of the Executive Yuan on January 20th approved the report to the National Government to withdraw the investigation case (see National Government Gazette No. 682, January 27th, 20th year). The so-called pretexts for requesting the central government to be lenient and exempt from further investigation are also not true.

A report was submitted to the Central Political Council immediately. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Wang Jingwei Described the Signing Process

(Nanjing) At the Central Political Council on the 23rd, with Jiang Zhongzheng presiding and Yu Youren absent, Wang gave a detailed explanation of the signing of the Shanghai ceasefire agreement, which stated that before the agreement was signed, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had reported the content of the agreement to the Executive Yuan and submitted it to the Central Political Council for review and deliberation. The council then discussed whether or not it should be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and decided that the situation could be notified to the Legislative Yuan by the Central Political Council, and Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Xu Mo reported to the Legislative Yuan on record. This type of agreement is different from the signing of international treaties. The impeachment proposed by the Supervisory Yuan was presumably due to a misunderstanding of the case. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

The Guangdong Naval Negotiations Have Broken Down

Chen Ce Refuses Reorganization. Chen Jitang Decides to Use Force

Zhao Guizhang Was Summoned Back to the Province to Reconcile and Appease the Navy

Air Force Generals Decide to Issue Another Declaration Not to Participate in Civil War

Chen Jitang Actively Deploys Defenses on the West River

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang generally agreed to Hu Hanmin's proposal to mediate the naval unrest, agreeing to divide the navy under the jurisdiction of the Jiangfang and Haifang command posts. In peacetime, the Haifang ships would be under the jurisdiction of the Political Council, and the Jiangfang ships would be under the jurisdiction of the provincial government. However, in wartime, the Haifang and Jiangfang ships must be under the unified jurisdiction of one group. Chen Ce was also asked to transfer all the land troops of Qiongyai back to the province for reorganization by the Political Council. Chen Jitang sent Chen Rong to Hong Kong on the 20th to meet with Hu Hanmin and present the above proposals. Hu negotiated with Chen Ce for two days, and Chen Ce believed that he could not accept them. Chen Rong returned to the province on the 21st to report back. Chen Jitang therefore decided to use force against Qiong and sent someone to Macao to welcome Zhao Guizhang back to the province to carry out the reconciliation and appeasement of the navy again. It was decided that Zhao would be given the position of naval commander if the matter was successful. Zhao has already returned to the province. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Postal Protection Movement Across Various Regions

Two Postal Associations Host Representatives from All Circles in Beijing

(Nanjing) This afternoon, the Nanjing Postal Workers' Union and the Jiangsu-Anhui Postal Workers' Union hosted over a hundred representatives from agricultural, industrial, commercial, academic, women's, overseas Chinese, news, legal, banking, and financial circles at the Central Hotel. Representatives Kong Fanzao and Wang Shushen respectively reported on the reasons and aims of the postal protection movement. They also explained the necessity of abolishing the merger of the postal savings and remittance bureau, ceasing the allocation of subsidies to airlines, postal economic self-sufficiency, implementing special accounting, and maintaining the postal system. Finally, they declared that the postal strike in Shanghai is serious. The position and responsibilities of the two postal workers' unions in Nanjing and the Jiangsu-Anhui region are extremely important. The workers' unions in various ports along the Yangtze River have always been under the leadership of this region, and their actions are sufficient to affect the overall situation. Therefore, it has been decided to adopt peaceful movement and reasonable methods to request the authorities to accommodate their consistent views and resolve the issue as soon as possible, so as to avoid the expansion of the incident. This joint movement is entirely for the purpose of protecting the postal service and has absolutely no other background or color. They hope that all sectors will provide assistance. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Ye Chucang Reports on the Grand Canal Project Issues

At the Central Government's Beijing Office Commemorative Week

(Nanjing) The Central Government's Beijing Office held Premier's Commemorative Week at 9:00 AM on the 23rd. Over five hundred people attended, including Central Committee members Zhang Ji, Ju Zheng, Ye Chucang, Chen Lifu, Shi Ying, and Zhang Qun. Ju Zheng presided. After the ceremony, Ye Chucang reported on the Grand Canal project issues, stating that last year's Grand Canal breach caused losses of over 50 million yuan to the people. The current expenditure of 3.5 million yuan for this project is expected to be completed by the end of the month. "We are very ashamed. Why didn't we repair the Grand Canal before the breach, avoiding such huge losses? It is easier to prevent things before they happen than to remedy them afterward. The people have suffered many losses in recent years, and we can only blame ourselves. We must break through the adverse environment and achieve our ideal goals. We must have active confidence, but on the other hand, we must have even deeper self-criticism. So-called confidence is confidence in the entire party, not in oneself. If we only believe in ourselves, it is worse than having no confidence at all. We also recall the relief of disaster victims. The central government has spent a lot of money, but there are still many victims in Henan and Shaanxi who have not received relief. Thinking of these difficult issues, we feel even more the great responsibility of our party. In the future, we cannot cope with the current difficulties without the strength of the entire party. We can never gain the sympathy and trust of others without constant self-criticism. In short, we can only overcome this difficulty and complete the mission of the revolution by having confidence in the party and self-criticism regarding our responsibilities," and so on. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Saito in Consultation to Form Cabinet

Japanese People Regard Him as Hindenburg the Second

Gathering National Talents to Join the New Cabinet

Reuters, Tokyo, 23rd The new Prime Minister Saito visited Takahashi today, reportedly intending to invite him to serve as Minister of Finance. Although this news has not been verified, it is sufficient to show that Saito is trying to recruit national talents, regardless of which party they belong to. At the same time, he seeks to connect the two major political parties to cope with the serious national crisis that Japan is believed to be facing. Although the candidates for the new cabinet are still unpredictable, Saito's handling of politics has won almost universal praise, because the public recognizes that the current difficulties can only be saved by a true leader who can unify the country like German President Hindenburg, who is not suspected of any party conspiracy, can gain the trust of the country, and puts national interests and people's happiness above everything else. The current disturbances across the country are not small in the minds of the people. Now, with a fair and honest politician like Saito as Prime Minister, he will surely alleviate the fears, and at least temporarily restore credibility. However, everything still depends on how the cabinet handles the current economic situation, and whether it can permanently eliminate hidden dangers. The agricultural area is particularly important, so the position of Minister of Finance must be carefully selected.

Hiranuma is internally set as Minister of Justice, Secretary General Kuyama Tsurukichi, Director General of the Legislation Bureau is either Arichika or Matsumoto, and the Superintendent General of the Metropolitan Police Department will be selected from among Akaike Ko, Goto Fumio, and Shibata Yoshisaburo. International Anti-War Congress

Scheduled to Convene in Geneva on August 1st

The Premier's Wife is Also One of the Initiators

國民社 (Kuomin News Agency) dispatch from Paris, 22nd: The International Anti-War Congress has been scheduled to convene in Geneva on August 1st. Its executive committee today appealed to men and women of goodwill throughout the world, regardless of political affiliation, to give full support to the Congress. One section of the appeal stated, "War has now broken out in the Far East. Japan has invaded China. Whether the results will lead to intervention in Soviet Russia or become a flood engulfing the whole world depends on how the work of this Congress shifts world opinion." The signatories to the Anti-War Congress appeal include Madame Sun Yat-sen, Professor Einstein, Romain Rolland, Tresca, Barbusse, Gorky, Sinclair, Mann, and many other world-renowned writers and scientists.

Havas dispatch from London, 22nd: The great scientist, German Professor Einstein, has been residing in Oxford for several weeks. He recently departed for Geneva with Lord Ponsonby, the chairman of the International Anti-War Congress, to jointly protect peace and justice. Many members of the Congress saw them off at the station platform. As Professor Einstein does not speak English well, Mr. Ponsonby made a statement to the press on his behalf, briefly stating, "We are going to Geneva in a private capacity, because public opinion is more accurate than the representatives of the disarmament conference. Our purpose is not only to observe how everything is proceeding. So far, the work of the disarmament conference is less about permanently eliminating war and more about jointly avoiding war. Global public opinion hopes for the success of the disarmament conference like a great drought hopes for clouds. If the conference fails, it will have an ominous effect on public opinion." Professor Einstein will first thoroughly study this problem and then propose practical proposals. He will return to England after staying in Geneva.

World's Premier Gold Nation Also Feels Economic Panic

Budget Deficit

Unemployment Rises Sharply

United States Fails to Devise Good Policies to Restore its Former Position

World Commercial Prosperity Will Never Be Revived. Reuters dispatch from London, 22nd: The United States, possessing half of the world's gold, which has long been revered as the foundation of its prosperity, is gradually showing signs of dissolution under the pressure of the current economic panic. Financiers and politicians are deeply anxious. World commentators are now offering advice on restoring sound policies. The United States occupies a gear-like position in the world trade machine. Only when the gear turns can the world trade machine operate. Therefore, the revival of Europe depends on the United States restoring its gear-like position. For this reason, although observers know that the fundamentals of the U.S. economic power will not be shaken and that its future recovery is assured, they cannot help but feel apprehensive about the increasingly serious situation in the United States. Some say that although the U.S. budget is currently in deficit by a large amount, it can eventually be balanced. More important than fiscal policy is the difficult problem of the large number of unemployed. The rule of law in the United States is solid, but actions that undermine the rule of law can also be taken at any time. If private charitable funding is exhausted, the future of the United States has very serious possibilities. Given the current situation in the United States, the amount of funds being withdrawn from the United States by foreigners is quite large. If this continues, all of New York's foreign exchange reserves will be completely depleted in a relatively short period. However, the United Kingdom, in accordance with the policy set by Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, established a pound exchange equalization fund to sell pounds and buy U.S. dollars, resulting in approximately 200 million yuan being deposited in the United States. This can offset some of the withdrawals by foreigners. The absolute collapse in the value of U.S. securities can be seen in the stock market listings. The face value of several major railway securities is approximately 200 million yuan, which rose to a high of 350 million yuan in 1929 but has now fallen to 28 million yuan. The U.S. railway freight business has also declined sharply. In the week before May 14th this year, freight cars transported 521,000 vehicles, while at the same time last year, there were 748,000 vehicles.

Search for Successor to the Premiership

國民社 (Kuomin News Agency) dispatch from Athens, 22nd: Today, the Greek labor unrest has made some progress. Since the authorities threatened striking leaders with military trials, postal workers resumed work this morning. Today, the newspapers published the full text of Prime Minister Venizelos's resignation letter to the President last night. Regarding the current situation, it stated that the civil servants' strike must be regarded as an attempt at revolution. He strongly advocated that Greece must be considered to be in a state of war until all work is resumed and order is restored everywhere. Finally, he suggested adding a clause to the constitution authorizing the President to temporarily suspend all civil rights, including the right to strike, if national security is endangered by the exercise of civil rights. This morning, the President and the Speakers of both houses of Parliament met for a long time. Subsequently, he summoned Tsaldaris, a political leader who is highly regarded by the people. Therefore, the President is expected to choose the next Prime Minister from between Panagiotis Tsaldaris, the leader of the United Republican Party, and General Kondylis, the leader of the National Republican Party.

Conflict Between Muslims and Hindus in India Gradually Subsides

138 Dead

1,600 Injured

Reuters dispatch from Bombay, 23rd: The conflict between Muslims and Hindus in India intensified again on Thursday, especially in the cotton mill area. However, it has gradually subsided since then. Although there are still occasional clashes here today, resulting in one death and seven injuries, the atmosphere is no longer as tense as before. The police have been working tirelessly day and night for many days and are now feeling fatigued. Therefore, the Governor of Bombay has called on local auxiliary forces and the Bombay Light Horse to assist the police in maintaining order. People are leaving the city one after another, mostly heading to Pune, from where they will go to the countryside. According to the official report released, as of Friday night, there were a total of 128 deaths and 1,600 injuries.

Chairman of British Steamship Company Passes Away

Reuters dispatch from Carlo, 23rd: Sir Owen Philipps, Chairman of the world-renowned British Steamship Company, died of illness on his yacht Rover today at the age of 79. Sir Philipps was a major figure in the world shipping industry and served as a director of many important companies. In 1901, he came to China to negotiate the Sino-British commercial treaty and subsequently signed the treaty in Shanghai on September 5, 1902. He was involved in many businesses throughout his life and also served in the government in India for several years. He was created a baronet in 1911, promoted to viscount in 1924, and further promoted to earl in 1929.

Important News

Extraordinary Cabinet Amidst Chaotic Political Situation in Japan

Eight Factions Compete to Rise

The Military Faction Generally Predominates

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun reports: At a time when national life is under pressure and the political tide is rapidly changing, talk of an extraordinary cabinet is being seriously discussed. Among those most active in this regard, there are eight factions. The first is the coalition cabinet movement led by Adachi. This faction has a number of strategists who are actively working to achieve this. However, the extent to which the public trusts party politics and the intentions of Saionji are difficult to predict. At present, the question of whether to reform political parties, reorganize political parties, or form a coalition of political parties is intertwined. Due to the urgency of the situation, the form of the extraordinary cabinet that will be formed is also a major issue in the near future. Those who are considered to be heads of the extraordinary cabinet are none other than Marshal Togo, Saito Makoto, Yamamoto Gonnohyoe, Ozaki Yukio, Izawa Takio, Ugaki Kazushige, and Hiranuma Kiichiro. However, there are also those who support the current Chief of the General Staff, Prince Kan'in Kotohito, and the Chief of the Naval General Staff, Prince Fushimi Hiroyasu. Those who support Marshal Togo are members of the Satsuma faction, following the precedent of Hindenburg in Germany. Saito Makoto has been actively working on the coalition cabinet movement since resigning from the position of Governor-General of Korea. Yamamoto Gonnohyoe also has the support of some people. Others, such as those who admire the Gakudo faction, have been promoting Ozaki Yukio, who returned from a foreign trip last year. However, among the young officers of the military, who are resentful of the corruption of established politicians and have changed their minds from the past two or three years of liberalism, many tend towards patriotism. Izawa Takio was rumored to be promoted after the reorganization of the Minseito. The above-mentioned views are confusing and have not yet been resolved. Recently, the Hiranuma promotion movement, which is called the Kokuhonsha and is linked to the Araki faction, and the Ugaki Major General promotion movement, which is linked to the military Ugaki faction and a part of the Minseito, have gradually taken shape. The central figures of the Kokuhonsha, such as Minister of the Army Araki, Minister of the Navy Osumi, and Ota Kozo, have absolute power. Hiranuma, who has no wife or children, lives a monk-like life in his private residence in Nishiohkubo, outside the city. Why does he get the support of various influential figures? Because Hiranuma, in addition to being the Vice President of the Privy Council, has a close relationship with the military centered on the Kokuhonsha. If Hiranuma rises to power, a powerful cabinet will be established with the backing of various military backgrounds. Countless other large and small politicians, surrounding Hiranuma and the Kokuhonsha, also want to join hands and rise up. Among them, Mori Kaku, the secretary general of the Inukai Cabinet, is the most blatant person. If the Hiranuma Cabinet is established, the Kokuhonsha will definitely have a strong mass movement. Moreover, when implementing policies after the formation of the cabinet, it is necessary to maintain a permanent organizational force. The established political parties will naturally be eliminated. However, it is feared that it will not be possible to raise the flag of a new political party in one fell swoop, as the established political parties have built their current base through more than half a century of struggle. As for General Ugaki Kazushige, there was a movement to join the Minseito in the past. Now, the Ugaki faction in the Minseito is linked to the Ugaki system in the military, aiming to succeed Wakatsuki with Ugaki. If Ugaki comes out, his regime will probably not belong to the Minseito in accordance with the usual constitutional path. Otherwise, under Ugaki, a cabinet of party alliances will be formed with the Minseito as the main body. However, it is also doubtful whether the anti-Ugaki system in the military can agree to it. In addition, the promotion of social nationalism advocated by Nakanono Seigo, who is active on the surface of the political world, the state socialism of Shimochu Yasaburo and Akamatsu Katsumaro, and the actions of various political factions such as the Greater Japan Production Party and the Patriotic Labor Party are also very fierce. Before the establishment of the new party, Nakanono Seigo traveled around the country, promoting social nationalism, which gained the sympathy of the people. However, Nakanono's political power is weak, so it is difficult to realize. In short, in this chaotic situation, each faction is doing its best, secretly leaping, and it is unknown who will win. It is worth noting.

Osaka Mainichi Shimbun The Imminent U.S.-Japan War Machine (Continued)

U.S. diplomat Lansing took the U.S. Secretary of State Bryan's protest to Japan during the Sino-Japanese negotiations in 1915, which was clearly aimed at protecting U.S. interests. However, Wilson in Paris and Hughes in Washington were no less than servants of China, catering exclusively to the psychology of the Chinese people, rejecting Japan's demands, and criticizing Japan's rights and interests. They used the protection of China's happiness as a banner, used morality as a shield, and skillfully wielded the gun of practical interests. This is truly the skill of American politicians in recent diplomatic history. No wonder the U.S.'s Far Eastern policy has been well-received by the Chinese people. Even Sun Yat-sen, who is comparatively thoughtful among modern Chinese people, regarded Japan as "imperialistic diplomacy" and the U.S. as "friendly diplomacy," falsely dividing the differences between Japan and the U.S., and training in the American method. As a result, the trend of rejecting Japan and flattering the U.S. spread almost throughout the country. Moreover, Shi Zhaoji, the former ambassador to the U.S., exerted his catering nature in the U.S. and concluded mining contracts for coal in Shaanxi and oil in Sichuan with American capitalists. On the one hand, he abandoned the promotion of the harmful and useless Anglo-Japanese Alliance and planned to form an A.B.C. alliance with China as the stage (A is America, B is British, C is China).

In the 20 years since the Russo-Japanese War, the U.S.'s attitude in the world can be said to be "grandly supporting China." Therefore, it is natural for them to strike a final iron hammer at Japan, based on their traditional vanity, to compete with Japan.

The relationship between the Manchurian problem and the U.S. is so complex. When the Manchurian Incident broke out, what kind of feelings did the U.S.'s attitude produce? Let us verify it with recent facts. (1) The current President Hoover, who is guiding foreign policy, has a utilitarian ideology at his core. Therefore, the U.S. is in a defensive position regarding the Manchurian problem. Miratu recently commented on Hoover, saying, "Hoover's thinking is originally that of a businessman, not a politician." Even today, ten years after he served as Secretary of Commerce, he still does not go beyond the scope of his utilitarianism. He is determined not to risk his own country's fate to compete with others for issues that are not important to his own country's existence. He is particularly unwilling to have active intervention because he understands the gains and losses.

Before the Manchurian Incident, the U.S. was in an unprecedented economic crisis in its history. The number of unemployed people increased sharply, and it was necessary to seek relief for local banks with weak foundations. The whole country was in a state of unease. President Hoover said in his speech at the Lincoln Memorial that he was now worried about the "visible enemy" more than the "invisible enemy" in the face of the economic crisis. Moreover, the current naval strength of the U.S. is inferior to that of the Japanese navy. If it wants to intervene, it must have sufficient and strong military force to protect it. Now that it lacks a strong military force as a backing, it cannot have any dignity. Intervention rashly without dignity will only lead to defeat. Therefore, when the Manchurian Incident broke out, the U.S. wanted to intervene, but it was not allowed by the situation. (To be continued)
