Min People Petition to Suppress the Communists

Dispatch Representatives to Nanjing to Meet Wang and Chiang

Please Immediately Transfer a Large Army to Fujian at Full Speed

Wait for the Official Announcement Before Returning to Shanghai

After the establishment of the Fujian Association of Shanghai-Based Organizations for Saving the Country, all work is progressing extremely tensely. A few days ago, Qiu Hanping, Zhen Yaogong, and Ge Jianxi were dispatched as representatives to Nanjing to petition. On the afternoon of the 20th, they met with President Wang along with representatives from the Shanghai-Based Association of People from Fujian. Wang personally received them. The representatives presented six key points of the petition: (1) Request the central government to dispatch a large army to Fujian to suppress the communists in the near future in order to save the people's lives. (2) Request the central government to send at least two divisions of capable troops by both land and sea in order to encircle and suppress the communists. (3) Request the central government to appoint a senior military officer to be responsible for directing the suppression of the communists throughout the province. (4) Request the central government to indicate the date of mobilization of the troops aiding Fujian in order to comfort the expectations. (5) Request the central government to provide disaster relief to the refugees in the disaster area in order to avoid displacement and being seduced by the communists. (6) Request the central government to earnestly purify the administration in Fujian and properly plan for the aftermath in order to eliminate the source of the chaos. Wang indicated that all of them could be accepted and said that the government was extremely concerned about the situation in Fujian and had decided to send three divisions of the most capable troops to Fujian at full speed in the shortest possible time and to appoint a senior military officer to uniformly command the suppression of bandits throughout the province. The representatives were satisfied and then excused themselves. Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, also received the representatives on the morning of the 22nd. The representatives are waiting for the government to make an official announcement before returning to Shanghai. As for Shanghai, Xie Yinpo and Xiao Bichuan have been recommended to contact various organizations and ask for their sympathetic assistance for Fujian affairs.

Shandong People Call for Yellow River Control

Please Help German People with the Cost of Yellow River Control

Please Allocate Boxer Indemnity to Repair the Lower Reaches

Jinan Dispatch: The flooding of the Yellow River is a major disaster in North China, and the provinces of Shandong and Henan are particularly affected. Every year, millions of dollars are spent on Yellow River control, but there is still the risk of breaches. The reason for this is that in the past, only prevention and blocking could be done, and fundamental dredging could not be carried out. The river water carries a large amount of sediment, which has been deposited for a long time. The riverbed is several feet higher than the ground. Once there is a breach, the water flows from top to bottom and cannot be stopped. Dozens of villages are immediately submerged. The losses over the years are countless. German Professor Engels is willing to use his recently established large-scale experimental field to provide experimental planning for Yellow River diversion. However, the required cost of materials and travel expenses of 22,000 yuan must be borne by the three provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan. The Provincial Government has already decided through political conferences to send a telegram to the governments of Hebei and Henan to negotiate and share the expenses. The Caozhou River Engineering Promotion Committee, which belongs to eight counties, has submitted a petition to the Shandong Provincial River Engineering Committee to present it to the Provincial Government as soon as possible to eliminate the huge disaster in North China. It has already been approved by the River Engineering Committee and will be presented to the Provincial Government in writing.

Li Baoren, a member of the River Engineering Committee, believes that the harm caused by the Yellow River is very serious in the lower reaches and should be fundamentally controlled at once. He specifically proposed to submit a petition to the Provincial Government to present it to the Central Government to allocate 800,000 yuan from the Boxer Indemnity to repair the dikes in the lower reaches in order to achieve a permanent solution. His proposal said, "I think that the lower reaches of the Shandong dikes are the most dangerous, and the reason for the danger in the lower reaches is nothing more than the low and thin dikes and the narrow and silted riverbed. In the past, Qing envoy Li Hongzhang was ordered to investigate the river and once奏准the method of treating the symptoms, and a major repair of the dikes was carried out. Since the founding of the Republic of China, more than 20 years have passed, the country has been eventful, and there has been no time for major repairs. Even in times of emergency, occasional repairs have not helped. Years of wind and rain have eroded and washed away, like a whetstone, it has not been seen to be damaged, but there has been a loss every day, and it is still as low and thin as before. Every time there is a strong flood in the autumn, dangerous situations arise. The constitution is weak, and the defense force is lacking. Therefore, in less than a few years, the Gongjia Dam incident occurred in the past, and the Wangji Hutantan also overflowed and broke the dikes one after another. The people's difficulties have not been alleviated, and the dikes are deteriorating day by day. It is estimated that the lower section of the south bank, from Putai Daoxu to Ninghai, and the north bank from Huimin Wuyangjia to Lijin, such as the Liu Tangjia, Li Tingzhuang, Fengjia, Wang Wangzhuang, and Laoguan Zhao Hanjia on the south bank, and the Laojun Tang, Lanjia, Zhao Jia, Temple Palace Jia, and Panjia Jiahe Jiangzhuang on the north bank, etc., are extremely short of water during a strong flood, and even the dikes are level with the water, or temporary sub-dikes are added, or various dangerous situations such as the successive emergence of small holes occur in various places. In addition, the riverbed is silted up, the tail is not connected, the amount cannot be accommodated, and it swells and spreads. If there is a slight oversight, it will immediately lead to confusion. Now, it is not easy to repair and expand, but it is doubly difficult to delay. It is proposed to start with the lower section, and the work should be doubled. According to the maximum water level, it should be 4 feet higher, and the top width should be 4 zhang uniformly. The dangerous work should be doubled. According to the maximum water level, it should be 5 feet higher, and the top width should be 6 zhang uniformly. In addition, the height of the sub-dikes added below Lijin in the autumn of last year is sufficient. If the increase is continued, the work can be completed in one fell swoop. It seems that the back of the dikes should be leveled uniformly again. If this is done, it can not only be done once and for all, but also turn danger into safety. It is estimated that a total of 800,000 yuan will be needed. At a time when the country is eventful and financial resources are tight, it is difficult for the provincial treasury to raise funds, and it is feared that the national treasury will also be difficult to allocate funds. It is found that the Boxer Indemnity will be allocated next time, and various water conservancy agencies are requesting allocation. The Yellow River in this province is also an important project. It is proposed to ask the association to present a case to the Provincial Government to present it to the National Government for approval, and to allocate the aforementioned 800,000 yuan from the Boxer Indemnity so that the River Affairs Bureau can engage in repairs in order to eliminate floods and protect the people's livelihood."

Wuhan Flood Prevention Continued Report

Torrential Rains for Weeks, Situation Critical

Recent Water Levels Continue to Rise

Hankou Communication: Here, torrential rains have persisted for weeks, and the river is rising rapidly. Wuhan, being the confluence of the Yangtze and Han Rivers, faces an especially dangerous situation. Citizens, recalling last year's tragic disaster, are filled with dread and fear. Initially, the Wutai Sluice Gate suddenly showed signs of danger. As the protection for Wuchang, it suffered delays in repair work, and the river water gradually reached the same level as the gate. Nearby residents appealed to the government. Provincial Chairman Xia Douyin and Construction Bureau Chief Li Shucheng personally inspected the site and confirmed the danger. They specially ordered Water Conservancy Bureau Chief Jiang Mingjing to expedite repairs, estimating that the work could be completed within ten days. If the water does not rise further, the situation can be turned from danger to safety. Secondly, the Hanyang dike from Black Mountain to Lanjiang is also planned for construction. According to the Water Bureau's budget, approximately 300,000 yuan is needed. Detailed plans are currently being drafted. In Hankou, the most important structures are the Zhang Gong Dike and the riverfront flood prevention dikes. The Zhang Gong Dike was previously contracted to the Fifth District Public Works Relief Bureau, but due to mismanagement, no progress was made. Recently, the river water is only a foot or so away from the base of the dike, making the situation very serious. It has now been transferred to the Post-Disaster Relief Committee for handling. Preparations for construction are underway, starting with an outer protective barrier to protect the dike body. Regarding the riverfront flood prevention project, a decision has been made by Chinese and foreign communities: the Chinese street and Special District One and Two will be the responsibility of the Post-Disaster Relief Committee; the Japanese and French concessions will be responsible for their respective areas; and the section below the Japanese concession will be the responsibility of the Pinghan Railway Bureau. Except for the Chinese street section connecting the Japanese concession and passing through Special District One, up to the connection with the French concession, which has already started construction, and the section in Special District Two and the section from Dakou Lane to the Jianghan Customs House, which are preparing for construction, the rest have not yet started. Due to the recent heavy rains, the river water almost reached the riverbanks in an instant, drawing some attention. On the 20th, Chinese and foreign officials and citizens held a flood prevention project meeting, urging progress on all sides. According to Chinese representative Zhao Huanzhang's report, the Special District One section is 70-80% complete and will be finished within a week. Other sections are being rushed, and all are expected to be completed within about a month. The Special District Three representative reported that the Chinese and foreign board of directors of the district approved a meeting of Chinese and foreign taxpayers to be held next Friday to raise funds for construction. The French Concession representative reported that the area is actively proceeding according to the construction plan. The Japanese Concession Japanese Residents' Association representative reported that regarding the project's progress, they are still awaiting government instructions, but when Special District Three and the French Concession start construction, the Japanese Concession will also begin at the same time. The Pinghan Railway Bureau initially seemed to have objections, but has now expressed its agreement. The bureau will be fully responsible for repairing the revetment from Chenjiaji up to Fenjinlu, requiring over 110,000 yuan. The landslide section from Fenjinlu up to the old Belgian pier will also be repaired in combination. If this section is taken over by the Post-Disaster Relief Committee, it will contribute over 25,000 yuan. All projects must be completed by June 12th at the latest, and must not be delayed beyond June 20th. (May 20th)

Furthermore, since the beginning of summer this year, rainfall has been excessive, and the Yangtze River's water level has continued to rise without end. On the 21st, the Jianghai Customs water mark was 32 feet, only 3 feet and 4 inches lower than the same day last year. Citizens are filled with panic. Yesterday, according to water conservancy experts, if there are no more torrential rains in the future, the water level will not rise as rapidly as it has. Even if it rises slightly, there will be no major obstacles. However, in the next few days, the water level will recede just as quickly as it rose recently. (21st)

Shantou Transport Union's Strike Against British Ships

No Loading or Unloading of Passengers or Cargo Since the 16th

Shantou Communication: The Shantou Transport Union, formed by lighter wharf workers, has historically received a "small labor fee" for loading, stacking, and storing goods in foreign firms and warehouses. This fee was calculated per item and allocated by the foreign firms to the union, amounting to approximately two to three thousand yuan per year. Last year, the British shipping companies Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire refused to pay this fee, claiming that it should be collected from the various storage shops. The union repeatedly negotiated with the two foreign firms without success. On the 12th, the Transport Union specially convened a representative conference of various unions, resolving to prepare for a strike and forming a 50-member investigation team to prevent Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire ships from loading or unloading passengers or cargo in Shantou. They also encouraged sailors to strike and disembark at the same time. However, this matter has significant implications for commercial traffic and local security. The municipal government has not paid attention to mediation. On the 14th, the Transport Union convened another representative meeting of relevant groups to discuss the tactics for the strike. They immediately resolved: (1) Starting on the 16th of this month, all work on Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire ships will be suspended. (2) Regarding passengers, because there are many waiting for ships in Shantou, the Hotel Association will first notify outbound passengers from inland counties to postpone their arrival in Shantou. Passenger disembarkation will be suspended one week from the 16th to avoid difficulties for passengers en route. Separately, the Overseas Chinese Mutual Aid Society, the Nanyang Water Passengers Joint Association, the Hotel Association, and others sent letters to overseas Chinese in Nanyang, Shanghai, and Hong Kong, urging them not to take the ships of the two foreign firms to avoid having no one to load or unload their goods upon arrival in Shantou. (3) If the issue is not resolved three days after Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson ships arrive in Shantou, the Seamen's Union will notify all workers to leave the ships. (4) Regarding other foreign firms or shops renting Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson warehouses, those who are paid by the customer for loading and unloading work will be allowed to continue working as usual. (5) Losses incurred by workers due to this strike will be investigated and reported by the various friendly associations for separate decisions. (6) If a satisfactory resolution is reached in this case, the various friendly associations should be notified first to discuss various plans for resuming work and handling the aftermath. Since the economic boycott against Japan in Shantou, almost all anti-Japanese businesses have been occupied by Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ships have disappeared from Shantou port for over two years. Therefore, this move will have a significant impact on Chaoshan commerce. (May 15th)

Songjiang Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Returned to Provincial Collection

The county government received a telegram from Provincial Chairman Gu, stating: "Investigating the tobacco and alcohol license tax in Jiangsu Province, it has now been decided by the Provincial Government's 489th meeting to be directly managed by Jiangsu Province. Any instances of disobedience will be investigated and reported." After receiving the telegram, County Magistrate Shen has telegraphed all district offices and the county chamber of commerce for verification and notification to all tobacco and alcohol merchants to comply.

Strange Colors Spotted in the Evening Sky

Yesterday evening around six o'clock, a ball of red light suddenly appeared in the sky, gradually becoming white, resembling an extremely bright magnesium light. It lasted for about twenty minutes before gradually disappearing.

Local Postal Workers Respond to Strike

Local postal workers, after learning of the Shanghai postal workers' strike yesterday, all believe that it is necessary to respond in order to achieve the goal of strengthening the postal foundation. Signs stating "Respond and Strike Unanimously" have been posted in front of each post office.

Suzhou Executes Ship Robbers and Deserters

The Shengze Banxin Steamer robbery case resulted in the arrest of seven principals, including Zhu Anbao, by the Third District Water Police. Four of them were executed on April 27th. Cao Shixiang was also sentenced to death by the Bandit Suppression Headquarters and executed by firing squad at the Wangshudun execution ground yesterday (22nd) at 10:00 AM. Furthermore, it was learned that the 60th Division Headquarters stationed in Suzhou executed a deserter named Cheng Fengting by firing squad on the morning of the 22nd.

Press Rescues Chief Editor of Major Newspaper

The chief editor Su Kuang (Xiao Su) of the local newspaper "Dabao" was arrested by the 60th Division Headquarters stationed in Suzhou. The reason for his arrest is unclear to outsiders. One theory is that Su colluded with local gangsters to plot improper activities. Another theory is that the newspaper published articles that offended Commander Shen. Representatives from the press, including Chou Kunfang, Wang Weigong, Hong Wuhong, and Yan Yisheng, were jointly selected to visit Commander Shen to inquire about the truth behind the arrest and seek his rescue.

Local News

Shirakawa's Life Hanging by a Thread

Seriously Ill Yesterday Afternoon at 2 PM

Vomiting and Passing Blood, Life in Danger

In a Comatose State This Morning

Japanese Commander Shirakawa was seriously ill yesterday, his life hanging by a thread. As of this morning when this newspaper went to print, he was still clinging to life. According to reports from the Japanese military hospital, Shirakawa's condition at noon yesterday was a body temperature of 38.5 degrees Celsius, a pulse of 98, and a respiration rate of 15. By 2:30 PM, he suddenly vomited blood and passed black-reddish blood, and his condition became critical. Hearing the news, officers from the Japanese Command rushed to his sickroom. Doctors immediately administered hemostatic injections and transfused 300 grams of blood. Shirakawa's consciousness was slightly restored. At that time, Acting Consul General Iguchi also arrived at the hospital to convey the Emperor's gift of wine. Chief of Staff Tashiro then arrived to convey the Emperor's imperial message bestowing the title of Baron. After Tashiro read the Emperor's message, Shirakawa drank a glass of wine and was still able to taste its deliciousness. Thereafter, his condition hovered between life and death, showing no signs of improvement.

First-Class Military Surgeon Sanuki Yoshihide from the Japanese Army Hospital was ordered by the Japanese Army Ministry to come to Shanghai to examine Shirakawa. He arrived in Shanghai on the Shanghai Maru at 3 PM yesterday and went to examine Shirakawa at 3:30 PM. At that time, Shirakawa was still able to answer silently, but his condition remained critical. The Japanese Navy Ministry telegraphed Commander Nomura at 5 PM tonight, ordering him to escort Shirakawa's remains back to Japan by warship if Commander Shirakawa unfortunately passed away. Whether he can escape danger tonight is truly in doubt. Important Japanese figures in Shanghai have gathered at the military hospital to prepare for any eventuality.

Jinghu Railway Fully Open Today

Two Round-Trip Trains to and from Beijing-Shanghai

The Jinghu Railway Bureau, because the Japanese troops at the Zhenru North Station have withdrawn before 11 AM yesterday, immediately sent personnel to receive the station at 1:30 PM yesterday afternoon. Regarding the railway track repair issue, due to the bureau's proper handling, the project progressed rapidly and was completed yesterday morning. It is now scheduled to open today with two round-trip trains to and from Beijing and Shanghai. Details are as follows:

Japanese Troops Completely Withdrawn Yesterday Morning

The Japanese troops stationed at Shanghai Station and Zhenru Station were not very numerous. Shanghai Station had only ten or so soldiers, and Zhenru Station had only twenty or thirty. After 10 AM yesterday, they successively withdrew to the headquarters of the military police. By noon, no Japanese troops were visible at either station.

Received Shanghai and Zhenru Stations Yesterday

The Railway Bureau had designated personnel to receive the stations yesterday morning. Shanghai Station telegraphed in advance to Yin Zhilu, the Western Section Engineer stationed in Nanxiang, to go to Zhenru Station at that time to handle the handover matters. After receiving the order, Yin, together with Chen Zhonghan, Chief of the Train Operations Corps; Chen Sicheng, Deputy Engineer; and Shen Shao, Suzhou Section Engineer, departed from Nanxiang by handcar at 10 AM yesterday and arrived at Zhenru Station at 11 AM. They reached an agreement with the Japanese troops stationed there. At 11 AM, our Ping An Security Team went to Zhenru Railway Station to take over. Yin then received the station. At 12 PM, he received MacKay Road Station and then went to North Station. The Japanese troops stationed at Shanghai Station withdrew at noon. At 11 AM, the Railway Bureau dispatched Li Zhaoyu, Station Inspector; Zeng Zhihong, North Station Master; Jin Zhu, Train Yard Inspector; and Rong Yi, Chief of the Police Corps; and Gong Guodong, Chief of the First Police Group of North Station, along with twenty or so police officers, and gathered at Meiyuan Road in the Fourth District of Zhabei. After Yin Tixin of the Takeover Committee reached an agreement with the Japanese side, they went to North Station to take over.

Director Chen and Others Inspect North Station

Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, Director Chen Xinghan, accompanied by Secretary Ding Zhenheng, Train Operations Director Zheng Baozhao, Deputy Director Yuan Shaochang, Works Director (Westerner) Drashus, Deputy Director Pu Dengqing, Accounting Director Ellis, Deputy Director He Yongyuan, Eastern Section Chief Engineer Feng Qili, Engineer Cheng Pengzhu, and Taweison of the China-British Bank, and others, went to North Railway Station to inspect the locomotive shed, ticket office, train operations office, and the damaged lower level of the Railway Bureau.

Losses and Repairs at North Station

Director Chen and the others returned to the bureau at 6 PM. According to those who went with them, all the items inside the North Station had been moved away, and all the glass windows on the station roof were broken, with none surviving. As for the Railway Bureau's headquarters, the second and third floors were almost completely burned down, with only the lower level remaining unburned. The bureau sent employees yesterday to clean up all the accumulated tiles, broken glass, etc., inside the station. It is planned to rebuild the second and third floors of the Railway Bureau's headquarters.

Jinghu Fully Open Today

Jinghu

The railway is scheduled to fully open today, with no obstacles from Shanghai to Beijing. Because vehicles loaded with gravel have already arrived in Shanghai yesterday, proving that there is no danger along the way, it has been decided to open today. The Railway Bureau's Train Operations Office will issue a notice today, the contents of which are as follows: "After the Japanese troops withdrew from North Station on the Jinghu Railway, it has been fully received and is scheduled to resume train service between Beijing and Shanghai today. Two round-trip trains will be temporarily opened. The first train from North Station will be a slow train at 10 AM, stopping at all stations, arriving in Beijing at 11 PM. The second train will be a special express train at 3:45 PM, arriving in Beijing at 11:23 PM. Also, the first train from Nanjing Station will be an express train at 7:30 AM, arriving in Shanghai at 4:46 PM. The second train will be a slow train at 8 AM, stopping at all stations, arriving in Shanghai at 9:05 PM."

Officially Open at the Beginning of the Month

After the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the Jinghu Railway bore the brunt, and the buildings on the railway between Shanghai and Kunshan were almost completely destroyed. Fortunately, all movable assets, such as vehicles and telephones worth 50 million yuan, were rescued before the incident by Zheng Baozhao, Chief of the Train Operations Office of the railway, who risked his life day and night to pull them out. After the Japanese troops withdrew yesterday, the press vehicles were able to travel from Suzhou to Shanghai, and the fact that the railway tracks and bridges along the way were unobstructed was entirely due to the Director of the Bureau Chen Xinghan, Director of the Train Operations Zheng Baozhao, and Director of the Mechanical Affairs Wang Shanshan, who supervised the planning in advance. It is now scheduled to open a temporary special train on the 25th, and officially operate according to the newly revised timetable from approximately June 1st. All offices at North Station will be temporarily located in the flat houses opposite the original site of the destroyed station. Furthermore, it is learned that the Railway Bureau's Train Operations Director Zheng Baozhao has recorded in detail the maintenance of traffic in the rear, the rescue of refugees, and the bombing of various stations after this incident. He has specially compiled and printed it, which was published the day before yesterday, and will be distributed to the transportation and news industries for reference.

Shanghai War Zone Post-Disaster Relief Committee Formally Established Yesterday

Committee Elects Deputy Chairman

Three Groups Established: Review, Relief, and Design

The Shanghai War Zone Post-Disaster Relief Committee was formally established at the Municipal Government at 5 PM yesterday. At the same time, the first plenary committee meeting was held, deciding on the candidates for deputy chairman and establishing three groups: design, review, and relief. At the same time, the Municipal Government instructed various bureaus to prepare consolidation plans separately to ensure progress. Details are as follows:

Meeting Situation

The Shanghai War Zone Post-Disaster Relief Committee held an establishment meeting at the Municipal Government at 5 PM yesterday. The first meeting was held at the same time, attended by Chairman Wu Tiecheng, Committee Members Shi Liangcai, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai (representing Shi Liangcai), Zhang Gongquan, Chen Guangfu (representing Zheng Jianfeng), Qin Runqing, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Yiting, Chen Bingqian, Guo Shun, Du Yuesheng, Shen Tianxin, Wang Binyan, Tang Chengzong, and ex officio members Wu Xuen, Hong Lanxiang, Wang Zengyou, Zhu Jiajun, Zhou Nianzu, Yu Hongjun, Yin Rugeng, Cai Zengji, Wen Yingxing, Huang Boqiao, Jin Liren, Xu Peihuang, Shen Yi, Hu Hongji, Mai Chaochou (representing Zhang Binghui), and nine others. Meeting Results

(1) Elected Shi Liangcai and Yu Qiaqing as deputy chairmen. (2) Passed the organizational rules, the full text of which was published last time, but Article 7 of the original text was amended to change the word "Chairman" to "Committee Chairman". (3) Decided to establish three groups: review, design, and relief. Candidates for each group will be discussed by the Committee Chairman and Deputy Chairmen and submitted to the next meeting for decision. Detailed rules will be drafted by the Municipal Government and submitted to the meeting for approval. (4) A thorough investigation of the war zone situation will be conducted. It was decided that the Municipal Government's relevant bureaus, together with the War Zone Post-Disaster Relief Committee, will conduct a thorough investigation as soon as possible (i.e., today or tomorrow) and report to the next regular meeting for discussion. (5) The regular meeting is scheduled to be held every Thursday at 5 PM. The second meeting is scheduled to be held this Thursday.

Instructions to Various Bureaus

The Municipal Government has instructed various bureaus regarding the war zone post-disaster consolidation matters: (1) In order to comply with the order, investigating the post-disaster matters in the Songhu War Zone, upon the Central Government's clear order, the Songhu War Zone Post-Disaster Preparation Committee has been organized, and the war zone has been successively taken over. Regarding the consolidation work, orders have already been issued to prepare plans and submit them for review. All revitalization matters in the city's war zone should be based on local conditions and needs, and detailed plans should be carefully prepared to ensure progress. In addition to separate orders, this order is urgently issued to the bureau to comply immediately, carefully prepare detailed plans within the scope of its jurisdiction, and submit them along with the budget within one month of receiving this document for examination and approval. This order. (2) In order to comply with the order, investigating the municipal consolidation expenses in the city's war zone, it has been submitted to the 202nd municipal meeting, ordering the Finance Bureau to raise 500,000 yuan to cope with the situation, which was resolved and approved. Now that the city's war zone has been successively taken over, detailed plans should be prepared separately to ensure progress. In addition to separate orders, this order is urgently issued to immediately comply, select the urgent matters that cannot be delayed and are within the city's financial capacity, quickly prepare concrete plans, and submit them along with the budget for approval. This order.

Establishment Meeting of Shanghai War Zone Post-Disaster Relief Committee (Photo by Li Zunyong)

Housing Consolidation

The consolidation plan prepared by the Works Bureau is as follows: (1) For houses that can still be repaired, they will be allowed to be restored to their original state, and the road line will be temporarily exempted. (2) For repair work with a larger scope, the owner may apply for the bureau to send personnel to guide the work, and the submission of drawings will be waived. (3) Houses that are too severely damaged and cannot be repaired in fact should be rebuilt. (4) The construction and new construction of houses will still be handled in accordance with the city's temporary building rules. (5) Within three months of the city's takeover, applications for house repairs will be exempted from license fees, but if construction is delayed for three months from the date of the license, the original license will be invalidated. Furthermore, the Works Bureau's consolidation plan has been filed by the Municipal Government, the text of which states: "Received and understood. The proposed measures for repairing houses in the war zone are still appropriate and should be filed for record and notified accordingly."

Verdict in the "Dahua Evening News" Case

The "Dahua Evening News," having not been published for long, was targeted because of its fierce language and attacks on the government. Ma Muya, squad leader of the political department of the French Concession police, discovered that the newspaper had not registered with the Municipal Council during publication, violating the publication law and the provisions of the French Consul. On the evening of the 9th of this month, he first went to Qinyi Printing House at 82 Gelaoke Road, arrested Fan Fuzhi, the owner of the printing house, and seized two sets of lead type and 1,000 copies of today's newspaper. Then, he went to No. 6 Huabao Lane, Huanghe Road, arrested Luo Gusun, the editor from Henan, and seized drafts and documents, taking them all to the police station and escorting them to the Second Special District Court for interrogation. These details have been recorded in previous reports. The case has been concluded after several trials by Judge Wu Fanglian. The verdict was issued yesterday afternoon: Luo Gusun was fined 150 yuan for publishing an unregistered newspaper, and Fan Fuzhi was fined 100 yuan for assisting in the publication of an unregistered newspaper. If they are unable to pay, they will each be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The two sets of lead type and 1,018 copies of the "Dahua Evening News" were confiscated.

Regarding the Extradition of Ahn Chang-ho

Reuters, Nanjing, 23rd: The Ministry of Foreign Affairs protested to French Ambassador Wilden regarding the arrest of Korean Ahn Chang-ho by the French Concession police in Shanghai for extradition to the Japanese authorities.

Taxpayers' Association Requests Immediate Withdrawal of Japanese Troops from Concessions

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council stating: "Respectfully, we received a letter from the temporary office of the Hongkou District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' Federation, stating: 'Since the outbreak of the Shanghai War, nearly four months have passed. The concession authorities have allowed Japanese troops to occupy and rampage, causing fear and panic among merchants and residents. How can they dare to open the market suddenly? The once prosperous market has now become desolate and unbearable. Who does not feel heartbroken? At this time of ceasefire and troop withdrawal, how can Japanese troops be allowed to rampage in the streets in groups of three or five? The committee of national defense forces should order the Japanese troops to withdraw immediately to restore the previous state so that merchants and residents can operate in peace. The citizens of Hongkou all fulfill their tax obligations and hope to restore commerce. Please send a letter to the concession authorities to negotiate as soon as possible so that the local area can be pacified as soon as possible. Please do not ignore this matter.' We are reviewing this matter. We also received a letter from the Shanghai Citizens' Federation stating the same reasons. Therefore, in the joint effort to restore normalcy, it seems that this unstable force that hinders the restoration of commerce should be removed by all means. Otherwise, who can guarantee that unfortunate events such as those on the south bank of Wuzhen Bridge will not happen again? All those involved are deeply concerned. Based on the reasons stated in the letter, we respectfully request you to investigate and handle this matter and provide a reply."

Continued Report on the Burning of the Japanese Ship

The Entire Ship Left a Hollow Shell

Many Military Supplies Lost

The Japanese transport ship Bombay Maru (yesterday's report mistakenly stated Guangfu Maru) caught fire at the Huangpu Wharf, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Further details are as follows:

Continuing to Transport Japanese Troops

The Japanese army in Jiangwan, Wusong, and Zhabei are all withdrawing. The Japanese Army Ministry has dispatched a total of eight troop transport ships this time. Four ships have already left Shanghai. On the 22nd, a regiment of infantry from the 18th Brigade of the Japanese Army, a battalion of infantry from the 19th Regiment, the 9th Battalion of the Aviation Corps, and a battalion of artillery continued to withdraw, transported by the Japanese ship Jiangsu Maru to the East. The remaining battalions are scheduled to be transported out on the 24th and 25th.

Cause of the Fire

The Bombay Maru, Harbin Maru, and others were all docked at the Huangpu Wharf in Yangshupu, preparing to load the first battalion of infantry, two artillery companies, the first battalion of the aviation corps, special forces, and communication troops from the Japanese 9th Division, which were withdrawing from Wusong and Zhabei. They were scheduled to leave on the 24th and 25th. Therefore, military gasoline, unused bombs, hand grenades, and heavy explosive bombs for aircraft were unloaded first. The soldiers had to board the ship today. While military equipment, ammunition, and gasoline were being loaded onto the ship, a fire suddenly broke out inside the ship at 7:00 AM on the 22nd. The cause of the fire is said to have been caused by sparks entering ammunition, causing it to explode and spread to the aircraft gasoline, causing the fire to become extremely intense and impossible to extinguish.

Fire Spreads Fiercely

After the Japanese Navy discovered the fire on the transport ship, fearing that there were still large amounts of military supplies, bullets, and bombs on the wharf, which were loaded into the Harbin Maru, and even more ammunition stored in the wharf warehouses, and that the fire would spread uncontrollably into the wharf or the Harbin Maru, creating a catastrophe, they sent ships to tow the Bombay Maru to the Jiangmian area near Gaoqiaosha to anchor. At the same time, the Customs fireboat and the Japanese Navy's fire extinguishers assisted in the rescue, but due to the excessive amount of ammunition inside the ship, it was difficult to extinguish it for a while.

Continuing Explosions

The ship has been burning since yesterday afternoon, for over thirty hours, and the flames have not subsided. Initially, only a portion was burning, but later the entire ship was engulfed. It couldn't be extinguished by spraying water, so the Japanese army let it burn. Even at noon today, the ammunition inside had not finished burning, so there were still extremely loud explosions at noon. After investigation, it was found that the large artillery shells and airplane bombs loaded on the ship had caught fire and exploded. Consequently, the fire re-ignited intensely in the afternoon. The interior of the ship, including the inner deck cabins and machinery, was completely destroyed.

Additional Transport Ships Dispatched

The Japanese troops in Shanghai were urgently awaiting transport to Japan. After the fire on the "Bombay Maru," it was confirmed yesterday that the entire ship was destroyed, including the engine, which was also blown up, leaving only an empty hull. The ship's losses are at least 400,000 yuan. This ship belonged to the Japanese mail company and was requisitioned by the Ministry of the Army. The military supplies destroyed in the explosion were worth over 100,000 yuan. Upon receiving the report, the Japanese Ministry of the Army urgently dispatched the "Tokiwa Maru" to Shanghai to replace the "Bombay Maru" in transporting Japanese troops back home. The withdrawing units are expected to leave Shanghai in the next two days. Yesterday, military supplies were still being loaded at the Huangpu Wharf.

Joint Association of Civil Organizations Opposes Clearing Confiscated Goods

Responding to the Supervisory Committee's Impeachment of Wang

The Joint Association of Civil Organizations in Shanghai held its fifth executive committee meeting yesterday. The important proposals were as follows: (1) To appoint Ni Yi-bao, Zhang Juan-sheng, and Wang Bao-zhen as representatives to contact civil organizations in various regions. Resolved and passed. (2) Regarding how to continue opposing the investigation and clearing of confiscated goods, resolved: (a) To convene a joint meeting of all organizations in Shanghai; (b) To advise the appointed members of the committee for clearing confiscated goods; (c) To appoint representatives to contact all sectors of society. Resolved: Wang Zhi-sheng, Yan Jin, Zhang Juan-sheng, Shen Zu-ru, Kang Xuan-yi, and others were appointed to make separate contacts. (3) Regarding whether the association should continue to express its position on the postal workers' strike, resolved: To publish a letter to postal workers across the country regarding the Shanghai postal strike. A temporary motion was made regarding whether the association should express its position on the Supervisory Committee member Gao You-tang's impeachment of Wang Jingwei. Resolved: (A) To send a letter to Gao You-tang encouraging continued efforts; (B) To send a telegram to the whole country calling for unanimous impeachment of Wang Jingwei. (Omitted) The association's advice to the members of the committee for clearing confiscated goods is recorded below: Sirs, In a letter sent to your committee on the 20th, our association offered six suggestions, which we trust you have taken into consideration. Given that the entire city is paying attention to this matter of confiscated goods, and that you have been appointed as members of the committee, suspicions are bound to arise. For your own sake, you should carefully consider your actions. Our association respectfully offers the following advice: Do not be tempted by great profits, do not act rashly, public opinion is a force to be reckoned with, public anger is to be feared. We hope you will give this careful consideration. Shanghai Joint Association of Civil Organizations.

Various Patriotic Associations Oppose Round Table Conference

Correcting the British Residents' Association's Proposed Declaration

The Shanghai United Association of Patriotic Organizations' declaration opposing Japan's collusion with foreign parties to undermine Shanghai's territorial sovereignty states: Since the September 18th Incident in 1931, the League of Nations Covenant, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Nine-Power Treaty, which all nations have adhered to, have been completely violated by the tyrannical Japan. Fortunately, world justice has not been completely extinguished, and friendly nations are still able to uphold fairness, so that the tyrannical Japan's territorial ambitions in the Eastern Provinces and Shanghai dare not be openly displayed. However, because the tyrannical Japan is constrained by the aforementioned international treaties, and its violent seizures cannot take effect in law, it is bound to use all sorts of insidious tricks to collude with a small number of foreign residents in Shanghai to conspire to promote a round table conference to establish a so-called free city. Enlightened friends from friendly nations will certainly not be used or swayed by them. However, we have recently seen reports that a British man named Huthwaite, in the name of the British Residents' Association, sent a letter to the chambers of commerce of various countries, intending to encourage the governments of various countries to convene a round table conference to resolve the future status of Shanghai. Disregarding international treaties, it is as狂暴 (wild and violent) as Japan. Our association believes that such propaganda is the greatest regret for Sino-British friendship. Shanghai is the Shanghai of the Chinese people. Except for the clauses stipulated in the Yangjingbang Regulations, the integrity and independence of its administrative sovereignty must not be violated by anyone. Not only is there the highest international charter, Article 10 of the League of Nations Covenant, to guarantee this, but also the clear provisions of Articles 1, 2, and 4 of the Nine-Power Treaty stipulate that the governments and people of all countries cannot agree or negotiate or understand in a way that infringes upon our country's territorial sovereignty. Recent resolutions of the League of Nations and the Hoover Doctrine of the United States all take this as their principle. We believe that British residents who advocate justice cannot obliterate this international charter and tarnish their reputation in the world. Moreover, during the riots in Shanghai in 1862, when foreigners used the excuse of the riots to advocate the establishment of a free city, the British Minister Bruce strongly refuted it based on international law and shelved the proposal. Who would have thought that ten years later, the advocate for the establishment of a free city would come from the British residents? This is certainly a small number of people who have been deceived by the tyrannical Japan, and we cannot but sigh for the British residents. As for the reasons given by Huthwaite, they are: (1) to resolve the management rights of roads built beyond the concession; (2) to eliminate the danger of Chinese troops stationed around Shanghai; (3) to improve the handling of litigation cases in the Special District Court. If a round table conference is not convened, it will be impossible to guarantee the safety of the concession. However, it is not known that the first point he referred to is a local matter. How to deal with it should follow the existing regulations, and there are local authorities to resolve it. How can anyone interfere recklessly without following the proper channels? The second point he referred to is not only harmful to the independence of our country's administrative sovereignty, but also obliterates the fact that the January 28th Incident was caused by the tyrannical Japan using the concession to station troops. If all foreign residents do not forget justice, they should uphold strict standards to punish the tyrannical Japan's destruction of the concession's security, then the peace of the concession will be guaranteed. Instead of doing this, they use the danger of preventing the stationing of Chinese troops as an excuse. May I ask, in the past decades, when have Chinese troops endangered the concession? This kind of pro-tyrannical Japan rhetoric is self-defeating. As for the third point he referred to, it is even more related to our country's sovereignty and does not allow foreign intervention. Moreover, since the establishment of the court, apart from a slight decrease in the income of a few foreign lawyers, there have been no other inconveniences. Our association cherishes our country's territorial sovereignty and especially cherishes various international treaties. If there are those who violate international treaties and endanger our country's territorial sovereignty, we will only maintain justice and fairness and deal with them accordingly. In order to awaken the attention of foreign residents in Shanghai, we hereby declare as follows: (1) The historical significance of the round table conference is for the mother country to deal with colonies. This kind of term insults the independence of our country, and we must not tolerate it. (2) The Shanghai Incident and the Eastern Provinces Incident are the entire problem between China and Japan. It cannot be resolved separately, and how to resolve it, we only trust the League of Nations Covenant and the Nine-Power Treaty in law, and we do not know others. (3) Shanghai is Chinese territory, and we oppose any attempt by anyone or any country to change our original administrative organization or administrative methods to infringe upon our sovereignty, especially opposing the round table conference that attempts to create a so-called free city. The above three points are our attitude towards the Shanghai issue. We hope that all enlightened foreign residents will severely correct Mr. Huthwaite's statement, and especially hope that foreign residents who are close to the Japanese will recognize the nature of Japan's atrocities this time and not make the mistake of acting like they are dividing the spoils. If unfortunately a few people are blinded by greed and willingly used by the tyrannical Japan, allowing Mr. Huthwaite's statement to continue to spread, then our association will lead three million people to fight to the death to protect the dignity of international treaties and the integrity of our country's territorial sovereignty. Even if Shanghai is reduced to ruins, we will never allow the so-called free city to appear. The seas may dry up and the rocks may crumble, but this will will not change. We hope that Chinese and foreign people will take note of this solemn declaration.

The Light Emitted by the Meteorite and White Clouds Last Night

There Was a Thunder-like Sound in the Sky

Regarding the strange and colorful white clouds discovered in the sky over this city last night, according to the North China Daily News yesterday, it was the light emitted by the tail of a meteorite. One and a half minutes after its appearance, there was a rumbling sound in the sky, like thunder.

The Water Company States the Reasons for the Water Meter System

The Shanghai Water Company's Secretary and General Manager, Walter, states the reasons for the water meter system as follows: Regarding the matter of creating a water meter system to calculate water fees, the Public Works Department approved it last year, and at that time, the Shanghai Property Owners' Association (International Association) and the Shanghai Property Owners' Association (Chinese Association) did not object. Why is it that there are now people propagating that its effect is to increase water fees? The above propaganda is inconsistent with the facts. According to the water meter system, its effect is that users can pay according to the actual amount of water they use, which is definitely not like the current system in homes, where water fees are calculated based on rent. The French Concession and Zhabei both use the water meter system, and this system is also common in the United States. Most European countries also use this system.

Some say that if a certain property is calculated using a water meter, the cost will increase fivefold compared to the current cost. However, according to the amount of water currently used there, compared to the price currently paid, it is actually more than five times higher. This matter has now been clarified. The amount of water used there is not for ordinary household use, so using this matter as the effect of using a water meter is an erroneous inference.

It is currently difficult to predict how much water will be used in any given place. It will only be clear after checking how it goes in the future. Therefore, users do not need to anticipate whether there will be any difficulties. If, in the future, the water fees using the water meter system are much higher than the current monthly fee, the reason should be investigated in detail at that time to provide proof. Moreover, if the property owner or tenant can cooperate with the company, they can always limit the amount of water used to a reasonable level.

The main idea of using a water meter is to avoid the waste of water. Its more distant goal is to be cheaper than the monthly fee system, and there is no extra profit to be made. The extra profit is determined according to the contract signed between the Public Works Department and the Water Company.

Also, some property owners intend to cancel the habit of property owners contracting for the water fees of a piece of property and install separate meters for each tenant when using the water meter system. However, this matter was fully studied when discussing the current water rate. However, according to the water rate before implementation, our company has the right to have the property owner of a piece of property be responsible for the water fees of that piece of property. This is a long-standing habit (and also for the French Concession and Zhabei companies). It is usually handled in this way. There are similar things in the United Kingdom and the United States. In new-style buildings with rented rooms, it is also common to contract for the water fees of each tenant in the name of the property owner. When implementing the new water rate, this situation was changed according to the requirements of some property owners. However, there are still contracts established with property owners. However, property owners have the right to have the company establish contracts with each tenant in any place. If so, the cost of changing the above-mentioned water pipes must be borne by the property owner, and a deposit sufficient to offset the value of the water meter must be deposited with the company. When the property is transferred to others or the water meter is removed, the deposit will be returned. Although the interest on the deposit is equivalent to the interest on the price of the water meter, the extra costs of maintaining the investigation number and collecting payments are subsidized from the water rate. Therefore, having the property owner responsible for the cost of changing water pipes and the deposit seems a bit worse at first, but it will become clear later. The cost of changing water pipes is actually in line with the money saved when the property owner and the company sign a contract. In other words, when the water pipes were originally installed, there was a method of installation that made it possible to establish contracts with each user. This only increased the original price of the water pipes. Furthermore, the extra cost of installing separate water meters for each household will ultimately increase the water price, and its benefits can only be given to a portion of the users. Therefore, it must be fair according to the various clauses listed in the water rate.

Also, property owners can first install a total water meter at each piece of property. According to all statistics and observations, the amount of water used in similar places and houses with similar rents is not the same, and the differences are very large. There is always a special reason for places where the cost of water is too high, so this must be investigated in detail. If the efforts of the company and the property owner to reduce the cost of water are still ineffective, the property owner can still install separate water meters for each user according to the above conditions if they want to do so.

If opinions are sought from various places in the concession, they would likely fully support the water meter system. For example, the Board of Water Commissioners of Petersborough (transliteration) in the United States stated in 1899, "Most users are reasonable water users and do not waste it. Only a few users, due to negligence or waste, release large amounts of water into the sewers. As a result, it will increase the amount of water that should be supplied and the water fees that individuals should bear. Therefore, the loss caused by the waste of water by a few users must be compensated by all residents of the city. If each user installs a water meter, those who waste it must pay for it themselves, and others can be exempted from paying for it. In other words, the water fees of others can be reduced." Also, in the 46th compilation of the annual journal of the American Society of Civil Engineers in 1901, Mr. Trotter Wana (transliteration) said, "Experts in engineering do not need to study the matter of limiting waste of water, and everyone would likely agree that the only way to limit waste is unfortunately that in most towns in the United States, the managers of the waterworks are managed by committees of laymen without expertise, and they often listen to the opinions of the majority who are ignorant." Also, the former general manager of the Paris Waterworks in France said, "Those who use water meters can use the amount of water they want, and the waterworks have permanent and the most accurate supervision. Therefore, users do not pay if they do not use water, and the waterworks can fully collect the price for all the water supplied." Also, in new-style buildings with rented rooms, the feelings of property owners and tenants when using water meters (in European and Western countries, this type of house is similar to a piece of house in China) on this issue, Mr. Hixon (transliteration) wrote a book on the price law of the water meter system of waterworks (in 1918), in which he said, "The total amount of water taken is the responsibility of the property owner. If the tenant wastes it, the property owner will suffer. Therefore, disputes often arise, and it is difficult to create a water meter system. Later, property owners gradually realized that the reason for wasting water was that the water equipment was damaged and leaking, and no one cared about it. Therefore, the water equipment is often repaired so as not to increase the water costs. Moreover, it is difficult to install separate water meters for each room (such as tap water and lights) because of the installation of water pipes, but it cannot be said that it cannot be done, but there is not much benefit." According to what is said above, it can be said that the difficulties of the Shanghai Waterworks are roughly the same as the difficulties of waterworks in other places. Therefore, adopting the water meter system in other places can solve this kind of difficulty, and adopting the water meter system in Shanghai may also achieve the same result.

When discussing the local water problem, attention should be paid to the interests of the shareholders of the waterworks, because their interest is fixed. Therefore, the price of the water sold is directly determined by the total cost of water production and transportation. If the total cost is high, the water price will also be high. If the total number is reduced, the water price will also be reduced accordingly. Therefore, adopting a method of increasing the total cost will directly increase the water price. Therefore, if separate water meters are forcibly installed in each small house, the cost of using water is actually not enough to offset the cost of installing, maintaining, and viewing the water meter. Although this is for the convenience of the property owner, this method is actually not economical, and the result will always increase the public's water burden. In other words, using an uneconomical method will actually cause the entire population to suffer losses.

The city is now divided into several small areas for the purpose of creating a water meter system. This matter has been explained before and does not need to be detailed again. In short, water meters will be installed in each area one after another. When the equipment is completed, water fees will be calculated using the water meter system. The equipment has now been completed in two areas, and new contracts have been sent. Most of the users in these two areas have signed and returned them, but there are also some who are listening to outside announcements and delaying to see what happens. It is hoped that these users will sign and return the new contracts as soon as possible to avoid future disputes. This would be greatly appreciated.

Streets Like Ghost Towns During the War

No Usage, Of Course, No Fee

Residents in the war zone have either perished in the artillery fire and blood-soaked fields or fled for their lives, enduring unspeakable suffering. Even residents of the concession enjoying the protection of the Public Works Department's police force, such as those in the Hongkou district, have been occupied by the Japanese army since the beginning of the Shanghai Incident. The entire district has fallen into chaos, enduring the ravages of war as if it were a war zone. Moreover, they have suffered even more from the killings and destruction by the Japanese army. These facts are widely seen and heard by both Chinese and foreigners. Now that the troop withdrawal agreement has been initially reached, residents are gradually gathering. However, the difficulties ahead are great, and recovery will not be easy. Therefore, our association and others advocate that during the war, since telephones and water were mostly unused, their fees should be exempted for one season altogether. This is the minimum requirement and not an unreasonable request. We have already informed the various branches to notify their members to suspend payment until a result of the negotiation is reached, in order to alleviate the merchants' difficulties and maintain the market." Upon investigation, the statements in the letter are indeed unavoidable facts. The motive for waiving donations and rents also lies in this. Logically, no fee should be paid if there is no usage.

Long Unresolved Labor Dispute at the Shishi Xinbao Newspaper

Since April 2nd, the authorities of the Shanghai Shishi Xinbao newspaper, citing the "Da Wanbao" incident as a pretext, have dismissed a large number of workers without cause. It has been two months, and the attitude of the employer towards the laid-off workers remains stubbornly unchanged. Feeling that there is no hope of resolution and under the pressure of life, they all went to the residence of Zhang Zhuping, the chairman of the newspaper, yesterday morning (22nd) to petition. At that time, Zhang was still asleep. The workers submitted a petition and waited for a long time before he instructed them to send representatives to talk. At that time, Zhang said that he understood the intentions of the gentlemen and others, but the words "return to work" were difficult to accept. He himself was only one of the directors of the newspaper and had no right to interfere with the newspaper's administration. The gentlemen and others could ask the labor union to negotiate with the newspaper's manager themselves. He then instructed the driver to pick up the newspaper's manager, Xiong Shaohao, and asked him to be responsible for negotiating with the labor union. The workers' representatives, believing that Zhang had agreed to negotiate, withdrew and reported to the labor union, requesting that representatives be sent to negotiate with the newspaper. It is said that the labor union immediately sent five responsible representatives to meet with the newspaper's manager, Xiong Shaohao. Unexpectedly, when the newspaper's manager met with the labor union representatives, he secretly reported to the police station to send detectives to closely monitor them, as if facing a formidable enemy. Although the labor union representatives argued based on reason, the newspaper still evasively defended itself, without any result.

Yu Bolu's Appeal Case Scheduled for Trial

Yu Bolu, the former district chief of the Fifth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who ordered police officers Lin Qingxiang, Liu Weicheng, Wu Zhanyou, and others to open fire on Baoshan Road in front of the district, killing civilians, was sentenced by the District Court. Now, Yu Bolu and others, dissatisfied with the sentence, have appealed to the High Court. Over Eighty Boxes of Military Supplies

Discovered by Water Patrol

Boatmen Repeatedly Evade Responsibility

Around 10:00 PM the night before last, a large sand barge suddenly docked at the waters off Wusongkou. Soon after, a pier boat and a rowboat sped in from the outer harbor and docked alongside the sand barge. This was spotted by Wu Minzhen, a sergeant of the Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who was patrolling the river. He saw that the pier boat and rowboat were loaded with a large number of wooden boxes, and the crew members were suspiciously transferring the boxes onto the sand barge. Suspecting foul play, he boarded the sand barge and conducted a search. He found two rifles in the cabin and pried open the wooden boxes one by one. Upon inspection, he found that they were filled with bullets. Believing that it involved the smuggling of a large quantity of military supplies, he seized the rifles, the sand barge, the rowboat, and the pier boat, along with more than eighty wooden boxes containing approximately 61,000 bullets. He also arrested the sand barge's crew members Zhang Gaohua, Zhang Xiaoqing, Chen Lin, and the rowboat's crew members Shang Qingyu, Zhang Xiaozhi, and others. When Liang, the chief captain, conducted a preliminary hearing, Tao Liufa and Chen Guangzai confessed that the wooden boxes were entrusted to them by a customer named Chen Xiangfu for transportation. Zhang Gaohua, Zhang Xiaoqing, Chen Lin, Shang Qingyu, and Zhang Xiaozhi all claimed that the wooden boxes were hired by a customer surnamed Wang in Wusongzhen to be transported to this location and unloaded onto the sand barge, and that they did not know that they contained military supplies, pleading for leniency. They were ordered to prepare documents to be submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

The Ephemeral "Security Donation Company" in the French Concession

The Security Company Cannot Provide Security

The French Authorities Insist on Thorough Investigation

The reemergence just the day before yesterday (the 22nd) of the "Security Donation Company" in the French Concession, suddenly discovered behind No. 8 Bu Nian Li on Rue du Consulat, almost shattered the quiet atmosphere of the French Concession in recent months and cast doubt on the resolute will that the French Concession authorities had always held. However, after the incident was revealed by this newspaper yesterday, the Chief of Police, Fébvre, immediately sent personnel to conduct a secret investigation and confirm the facts. Then, around 10:00 AM, he specially dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to search and arrest the perpetrators. Ten employees of the fake company were arrested on the spot, and more than ten account books and many national emblems and documents were seized. The signboard of the "Security Company" at the entrance was pried off and taken to the police station. After the head of the police questioned them one by one in detail, he ordered them to be detained separately to await trial in the Special Court. Since the case occurred, there has been much public discussion, with some saying that unscrupulous people were collecting money under false pretenses and others saying that negotiations had not yet taken place. Although these are just unfounded rumors, it is an undeniable fact that the French Concession has been strictly enforcing the ban on opium in recent months. Now, in the midst of this strict prohibition, such an illegal company has been established, and the location of its establishment is just a stone's throw from the police station in Bu Nian Li. It is said that the authorities attach great importance to this case and insist on a thorough investigation in order to get to the bottom of the matter.

Bizarre Homicide in a Kitchen

Qing Wu's Life Story Fragmented

West District and Zhang Engaged in Deadly Fight

Zhang Fu (also known as Zhang Fulang), who lived in the kitchen of No. 392 Chongqing Road in the New Concession, and the woman Zhang Wu retired to bed on the twelfth of this month at ten o'clock. The following morning they still had not stirred. At four o'clock in the afternoon, Zhang's friend Wang Heshang discovered Zhang dead on the floor in the room, while Zhang Wu was still lying unconscious in bed. The room was extremely messy, with broken bowls scattered on the floor. The responsible New Concession Police Station, upon receiving the report, sent detectives to transport the deceased to the morgue, where it was determined that he had died from injuries sustained in an attack. The woman was sent to the hospital for diagnosis. When she regained consciousness, she was transferred to the First Special District Court. Interrogation yielded no results, and she was ordered to be detained for further investigation. These details have already been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the woman is over forty years old and not particularly attractive. She originally lived with her husband, Mr. Wu, in Anting. Unfortunately, Mr. Wu died of illness in his hometown on September 1st of last year. The woman became a widow, and within two months, her son also passed away, leaving her with only two daughters, one fifteen years old and one eleven years old. Due to poverty, it was difficult to survive. The woman brought her two daughters to Shanghai last winter to make a living. She was introduced to work for the Du family at No. 66 Hehefang. Her two daughters, both petite and lively, were loved by their employer and were also kept as maids. Since then, they have not had to worry about hunger and cold. Around the first month of the lunar calendar, a hairdresser named A'er used her eloquent tongue to introduce Zhang Fulang, a Chongming native from the Wufuzhai pastry shop on Rue Guillaumme Brenier in the French Concession, to live with the woman. Zhang, who was about the same age as Wu, was like a thirsty man meeting water, while Wu was a newly widowed woman. After A'er's persuasion, they quickly became inseparable and rented a kitchen at No. 392 Chongqing Road to realize their love. Zhang had been a clerk at Wudingzhai for four years, earning a monthly salary of twelve yuan, which was more than enough for his personal expenses. After living with Wu, he inevitably felt that his income was not enough. In order to increase his income, he hired a substitute to replace him at the pastry shop, while Zhang and Wu set up a noodle stall on the side of the street. They had just started operating on the twelfth of this month when, unexpectedly, this unofficial couple did not embrace each other when they went to bed the next night. According to Wu's statement to the police station after regaining consciousness, she and Zhang had finished washing their feet and went to bed at ten o'clock on the thirteenth night. About an hour later, she heard someone calling Zhang's name outside the room in her dream. She got out of bed and opened the door, and suddenly saw two people rush in and beat Zhang severely. At that time, she was so shocked that she fainted and did not know anything about being arrested and so on. Now her nerves have fully recovered, and she denies having had a fight with Zhang Fulang. The head of the police sent detectives to investigate the other residents of the house, who all said that they had not heard any movement in the kitchen that night, and that the back door of the house had been tightly closed from 12:00 AM on the thirteenth night to 5:00 AM the next morning. If someone had entered from the outside, they would have had to pick the lock. After the police investigation, they concluded that the woman's statement was difficult to believe, and based on the messy state of the room, it was likely that they had fought with each other. Therefore, they charged the woman with the crime of assault leading to death in the First Special Court. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng interrogated her. First, Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, presented the case, followed by a Western detective who reported on the investigation. Then, the second landlord of the house, surnamed Jiao, and a fellow resident, Wang Shigui, testified that they had not heard any noise in the kitchen that night. Afterwards, Judge Feng questioned the defendant, Zhang Wu, who recounted the entire story of bringing her daughters to Shanghai to work as maids and her subsequent union with Zhang Fulang. Later, when her eleven-year-old daughter was also brought to the court, the woman was overwhelmed by the misery of her life and burst into tears. Judge Feng, believing that the case still required investigation, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing.

Chen Shuren Prepares for American Art Exhibition

To Be Held in Berlin

A reporter from the Riri News Agency interviewed Chinese Committee Member Chen Shuren at his residence in Beijing and learned that Chen and others are preparing for the Berlin Chinese Art Exhibition and Mr. Chen's solo exhibition, which will be held in China and abroad in the near future.

Evaluation of Chinese Art　Mr. Chen said that Chinese art is broad and profound, and is sufficient to represent the characteristics of Eastern culture. It is indeed praised by Europeans and Americans. After the Belgian Exposition two years ago, the only art that was praised more was French, then Belgian, then Chinese. This proves the importance of the status of Chinese art in the international arena. Last spring, the Chinese artist Liu Haisu held a Chinese modern exhibition at the University of Frankfurt in Germany, and then moved it to the exhibition hall in Heidelberg in the summer, arousing Europeans' deep attention to Chinese art. Because at the beginning of the spring of that year, the Japanese had held a large-scale exhibition in Berlin, but most of the works in it were made to cater to Europeans, so Europeans felt that Japanese art was merely superficially Europeanized and did not see its unique strengths. When they saw Chinese modern art, they were surprised and praised it, and all newspapers competed to praise it, winning a lot of honor.

Motivation for the Berlin Exhibition At that time, the person in charge of the Chinese Embassy in Germany suddenly felt the need for China to hold a Chinese art exhibition in Berlin, and formally agreed with the German National Art Academy to hold a large-scale Chinese art exhibition at the Berlin National Art Academy in February 1934. The German side has elected ten committee members who are all famous figures in the country's art world. On the Chinese side, the Minister of Education, the President of the Academia Sinica, the Chinese Ambassador to Germany, and Liu Haisu, Ye Gongchuo, and I were initially appointed as committee members. The other six members will be appointed after the Ministry of Education and the Academia Sinica jointly form a preparatory committee. The Chinese Embassy in Germany once sent a detailed account of the reasons by telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Education, and the Academia Sinica. Later, it was decided that the Ministry of Education and the Academia Sinica would be responsible for handling the matter, and it was requested that the Executive Yuan allocate funds for preparation. At that time, Mr. Liu and I would be given the opportunity to go to Berlin in person, if possible, and we also planned to transfer to Paris and London to exhibit and promote them, so that foreigners would have a more refined understanding of Chinese art. Regarding the method of collecting exhibits, we are preparing to widely collect the works of famous artists in the country, so as to form a spectacular exhibition, with the aim of creating a unique bloom of Chinese art in the world.

Solo Art Exhibition　I held a solo art exhibition in Guangzhou last year. It lasted for five days, and more than 50,000 people visited it. All the exhibits were eagerly sought after by the viewers. Although I politely declined to sell them because I was reluctant to part with them, the enthusiasts insisted on buying them. In the end, I reluctantly sold more than 20 pieces, worth about 10,000 yuan, but the best ones were not sold. At that time, the consuls of various countries in Guangzhou and foreigners paid special attention to them, and some even came early to request a special opening for one hour. The newspapers in Hong Kong and Guangzhou all published special editions dedicated to this news, which shows that Chinese and Westerners have a very strong interest in appreciating Chinese modern art. For the sake of popularizing the introduction, I plan to transport all my works, more than 100 pieces, from Guangdong to Beijing after the plum rain season, and then hold an official exhibition in the capital, and then go to Shanghai and then to Peiping, each place exhibiting for five days. These exhibits are the result of my years of experience in the Yellow River, Yangtze River, and Pearl River basins, and all the local landscapes and customs are incorporated into the paintings, especially the Guilin landscapes in Guangxi. My move is not to seek fame or praise, but to arouse the interest of Chinese people in art research. As for the effect and evaluation, I will transport them to Europe and the United States for phased exhibitions, because art is enough to promote the true spirit of the nation and express the inherent culture of the country.

Ding Xingzi Sentenced for Stabbing His Aunt to Death

To Serve Eleven Years of Imprisonment

Ding Xingzi from Yangzhou, resenting that his wife, Mao Guiying, a woman from Hubei, was introduced by his aunt Gao Xushi (also known as Xu Huiqing) to have a relationship with a certain adjutant, which caused Guiying to want to break away from her relationship with him and used the excuse of entering the church for spiritual cultivation, took advantage of his drunkenness at noon on the 3rd of this month and stabbed Gao Xushi in the abdomen with a knife in the pavilion of his house at No. 195 Dong Youheng Road, which led to her death after unsuccessful medical treatment. Mao Guiying and her mother, Mao Gao, were also stabbed in the forehead and hands. Ding was arrested by Liu Zhaonian, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station, and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and sentencing. The details have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over the first trial, and Ding Xingzi was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment for the crime of murder, seven years of imprisonment for killing a collateral relative, and five years of imprisonment for the crime of attempted murder. He should serve eleven years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the final judgment will be offset by two days of imprisonment for one day. The murder weapon, a knife, was confiscated.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather off the Shandong coast is unsettled, with strengthening cyclones, due to a Mongolian low pressure passing through northern China and moving eastward.
