Letter to the Editor

To the esteemed Editor,

I have recently read in the local news section of your esteemed newspaper about the discovery of a large batch of military supplies at No. 2, Lane 29, Fushantang Street. Upon investigation, there has been absolutely no such incident at our four houses. It is actually a mistake concerning No. 5, Southern Head, Sheep Intestine Lane, north of our location, belonging to Delu. As this concerns our reputation, I am writing to request that this letter be published in the "Letters to the Editor" section to correct the error, in order to avoid misunderstandings. Yours sincerely, Wang Zhuojun, May 23.

Dear Sir,

Regarding the item in the Shanghai Municipal Council's administrative records published in your newspaper on the 20th of this month concerning the waterworks investigation, there is a sentence stating that the Director of Public Works found it "inconvenient to add criticisms" to the experts' report. Please note that "add criticisms" should read "add opinions". I am writing to request that you kindly make the correction. Yours sincerely, Information Office, Shanghai Municipal Council, May 23, 1932.

Dear Sir,

According to Mr. Li Guangqin, the manager of the Jingzu Office of the Qian Yuan Industrial Company, I have recently read a news report in various newspapers about the Public Security Bureau seizing military supplies, which is inconsistent with the facts. This morning, the gatekeeper of Xinming Lane, Shen Zhubing, reported to me that six boxes of heavy objects, large and small, were discovered under the stairs in an empty house at No. 27, Miaoqiao Road, and he did not know what they were. I immediately went with him to investigate and reported the matter to the Chenjiaqiao Police Station. Police officer Sun Changrong came and used an iron tool to open the boxes, which contained prohibited military supplies. The police station then sent Chief Liu and other officers to transport the prohibited items to the bureau to avoid danger. The details reported in the news are mostly inaccurate. I have been asked by a lawyer to write to request a correction. I am writing on behalf of my client to request that your newspaper publish a correction to ensure accuracy. Yours sincerely, Zhou Shi Bi, Lawyer, May 23.

Education News

Important News: National Compilation and Translation Bureau Improves Textbooks

Engaging in Translation Work

Researching Natural Sciences

After the organizational regulations of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau were promulgated by the Ministry of Education, the internal organization has been largely determined. The following is a selection of the bureau's recent work and future plans: (1) Improving primary and secondary school textbooks. Although primary and secondary school textbooks have been reviewed in the past, it is now felt that they are not entirely suitable and that standards need to be revised and improved. The plan is to invite experts to critique the textbooks that have already been reviewed, select the better ones among the published books, conduct in-depth research, consider the pros and cons, and make supplements to improve them. It is also hoped that those who edit textbooks will not be bound by the standards set by the Ministry of Education, but will instead be divinely inspired, so as not to be as rigid as the eight-legged essays of the imperial examination era. Some aspects of improvement can be mentioned briefly, such as the scope of analysis of geology and minerals. In the past, secondary school textbooks provided detailed descriptions of minerals, but little research on geology. In fact, our travels through mountains and rivers, our archaeological studies of the past and present, make the study of geology even more necessary. It is heard that the bureau has invited Dr. Wang Gongmu to preside over the research on geology and minerals. As for history, the bureau plans to compile textbooks of extended length for university use. By shortening the long version, it can be used as a secondary school textbook, and by further shortening the secondary school textbook, it can be used as a primary school textbook. This cycle can also be consistent. It is heard that this compilation will be presided over by Messrs. Fu Sinian, Gu Jiegang, and Zheng Hesheng. (2) Translation work. This translation work has little foundation. Since the establishment of the Translation Committee, considerable work has been done. It is heard that, in order to be cautious about pharmaceutical terminology, Mr. Weng Zhilong will review it in detail before it can be published. Mr. Zheng Zhenwen is working on chemistry and plans to review it at the chemistry conference during the summer vacation. Physics is being organized. Biology is currently in the preliminary stages of work. (3) The bureau plans to contact university professors and specialized personnel to compile basic science textbooks for secondary schools and universities in the field of natural sciences, such as science. In the field of social sciences, it plans to compile and introduce more about international politics and international economics. It is heard that the bureau plans to appoint Mr. Chen Kezhong and Mr. Tong Guanxian as the heads of natural sciences and social sciences, respectively.

Local News

Jinan University Recovers Zhenru Campus

Inspecting and Photographing Each Location for Sealing

Strict Entrance Control, Striving to Restore Order

Yesterday afternoon, the Japanese troops withdrew from Zhenru, and the area was taken over by the Shanghai Ceasefire Zone Reception Committee. The most important institution in the area is National Jinan University. Therefore, at 9:00 AM yesterday, the university sent more than ten members of the university's Post-War Reconstruction Committee, including Fan Shouzhi, Yang Yufen, Zhang Tianfang, Lin Zhiying, and faculty and staff, to receive the campus with the Reception Committee. It was found that all the school buildings and equipment were badly damaged, especially the science building, which was destroyed by Japanese aircraft, resulting in even greater losses on the right side. After taking over, the university immediately raised the flag of the Kuomintang and the national flag, inspected and photographed each location for future reference, and sealed them separately. In accordance with the Reconstruction Committee, a plan for reconstruction and restoration was drafted and implemented step by step. In order to ensure strict entrance control, the school gate and the surrounding areas were guarded by police officers. Any faculty or students returning to the Zhenru campus for observation must first obtain a temporary pass from the Shanghai campus and present it to the police for verification before entering. Moreover, no one is allowed to take any items out of the campus at this time. They will be temporarily handed over to the custodians for safekeeping and returned at a later date. It is estimated that the restoration work will take two months to restore the original condition. In addition, President Zheng of the university also visited the campus for an inspection at noon on the same day and gave detailed instructions on the restoration matters.

Shanghai University Scheduled to Move Back to Yangshupu

Shanghai University, formerly located on Jungong Road, changed to opening and holding classes in the city center district due to the inconvenient transportation during the extraordinary situation. Temple Bell Ringing Records (IV) Not Removing Courtyard Grass Studio

(6)

The stars in the sky are constantly moving. Every day, they rise from the east, pass through the meridian where I stand, and head west. I compared the clepsydra with the stars and saw something very strange. I took a large bamboo tube, two feet long, with both ends open. At the outer end, I used a silk thread to make a diameter and glued it tightly to the tube to divide the tube opening into three semicircles. Then I placed this bamboo tube on a frame with the silk thread aligned with the meridian, so that the bamboo tube could be turned up and down. When a star approached the meridian, I turned the bamboo tube up and down to aim at the star. When the star reached the silk thread, I checked which grid the water in the clepsydra had dripped to. Strangely, in fifteen days, this star reached the meridian one hour earlier. In one month, it reached the meridian two hours earlier. In twelve months, it reached the meridian twenty-four hours earlier.

At first, I suspected that there was something wrong with the clepsydra. Later, a tourist stayed in our temple for seven days. He brought a round and flat monster. He said that this monster was called a watch. The short hand rotated once every half day for twelve hours, and the long hand rotated once every hour for sixty minutes, without any error. I used the watch to track the time when the Tian Shu star of the Big Dipper passed through the centerline of the bamboo tube opening every day. I found that the Tian Shu star passed through four minutes earlier each day. This was consistent with the result of comparing it with the clepsydra. It was four minutes earlier each day, which was exactly one hour in half a month. Later, another guest brought a more sophisticated watch that could report every minute and every second. After testing this thing for a few days, I found that each star reached the meridian three minutes and fifty-six seconds earlier on the second night than on the first night. Multiplying this number by the number of days in a year, 365 days, 5 hours, 48 minutes, and 46 seconds, it was almost a total of twenty-four hours earlier.

Why am I being so long-winded? Because the reason why my evening bell can be rung on time is entirely due to this point. First, I look north to find the Big Dipper. Then, I find the Tian Shu and Tian Xuan stars in the Big Dipper. If the handle of the Dipper is pointing to the right, Tian Shu and Tian Xuan are on the far left, with Tian Xuan in the south and Tian Shu in the north. Then, I draw a line from Tian Xuan to Tian Shu and extend it five times longer to encounter the North Star near the North Pole. Then, I use the North Star as the center to observe the rotation of the line connecting Tian Shu and Tian Xuan to estimate the twenty-four solar terms of the year and the twenty-four hours of the day. For convenience, I took a large iron ring that a child plays with and used twelve lines to make the twelve diameters of the iron ring, each intersecting at the center of the ring at equal angles. These twelve intersecting lines divide the iron ring into twenty-four equal parts, each equal part being fifteen degrees. I draw "a direction" every fifteen degrees, for a total of twenty-four directions. The four cardinal directions are east, south, west, and north. Then, I align the intersection point of the ring center with the North Star and make the north and south points coincide with the meridian. Then! East is on the right hand, and west is on the left hand. Then, I see which direction in the ring the line connecting Tian Shu and Tian Xuan falls on. As long as I know what solar term it is, I know what time it is. As long as I know what time it is, I know what solar term it is. For example, at 8:00 PM, the line connecting Tian Shu and Tian Xuan is in the southeast during the vernal equinox, then it is due south during the beginning of summer, southwest during the summer solstice, due west during the beginning of autumn, northwest during the autumnal equinox, due north during the beginning of winter, and northeast during the winter solstice. The same is true for this estimation. The stars travel fifteen degrees per hour, and move one hundred and twenty degrees every eight hours. If it is in the south at 8:00 PM, it will definitely be thirty degrees west of north at 4:00 AM. As each day passes, the stars, including the Big Dipper, are in the far north and not easy to see, so I use Wang Liang as a replacement. It reaches the meridian three minutes and fifty-six seconds earlier. If observed at a fixed time, this star moves less than one degree (more than fifty-nine minutes) from east to south to west. It moves fifteen degrees every solar term. Therefore, the time for ringing the bell every night is determined by the position of the stars. Everyone must be a little impatient. I have said all this just to show that I dare not be negligent in the slightest when entrusted by everyone to perform this bell-ringing duty. I know that my method, strictly speaking in astronomical terms! It still cannot be regarded as the most accurate. But within the realm of possibility, this country child has tried his best. Of course, I am still pursuing the most accurate way to ring the bell.

Shanghai Education After the January 28th Incident (IX) Still

XIV. Educating Refugees

The discovery of traitors is invariably due to the hardships of people's livelihood and the effect of ignorance. If we have statistics on traitors, we can prove that if we patiently guide them, it is not difficult to save them. People are not wood or stone. How can they clearly understand the great path and willingly be slaves and plunge their descendants into eternal destruction? The Shanghai Education Bureau, in view of the fact that most of the refugees in various shelters are adults who have lost their education and children who have no occupation, are easily prone to idleness and bad habits, iron errors in their thinking, and enter into misunderstandings. It is not difficult to be without them. Therefore, a "Refugee Education Committee" was organized to remind the displaced compatriots of their patriotism and to make them recognize the "nation as an eternal and immortal state" as said by the German patriotic philosopher, to provide spiritual training, and to cultivate the hearts of the people. In addition, efforts are made to implement general education, literacy teaching, and the inculcation of common sense.

The Refugee Education Committee was established in mid-February, with a total of twelve members. They prepared a sum of money and did the grassroots work in a practical manner. They found that there were as many as eighty-two refugee shelters in Shanghai, with more than 2,700 disaster victims. The twelve members used their spare time to prepare suitable educational materials and published three-color day reports. They took the teaching materials and went to the shelters to teach the refugees. On average, each person could visit two shelters per day, and the teaching time was about one or two hours each time. Every week in the morning, the members held a meeting to discuss matters that should be promoted or abolished.

The picture they published was very welcomed by the refugees. It is said that the painter Zhang Meisun was responsible for the picture, and the writer Yao Sufeng explained it in simple words, such as describing Shanghai's position, Shanghai's hustle and bustle, the enemy's situation, killing and arson, inhumanity, and the necessity of our resistance, etc. The second lesson of the third issue of the pictorial was a picture of displaced people, with the words "People with homes become homeless, people with money become penniless, many people lost their lives, many people have no food to eat". These few words can deeply stimulate the displaced refugees who have no homes to return to and are heartbroken by the scenes, which is very effective.

Sacrifice the price to benefit the students. It is heard that Principal Chen Hong is actively preparing to open the school as soon as possible.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Market: Rapid and Sharp Rise of 13.1 Taels

Surpassing 730 Taels: Yesterday, the 23rd, the gold price soared, surpassing 730 taels without significant fluctuations. Trading hovered around 5 taels both before and after noon, ultimately surging by 13 taels. The peak occurred early on, primarily due to repeated declines in the silver market and the formation of the Saito "super-party" cabinet in Japan. The general sentiment was that international crises were unlikely, strengthening confidence. Buyers were excited, and short sellers rushed to cover. Foreign exchange was also brisk but with slight fluctuations, causing gold prices to fluctuate by 2-3 taels at times. The afternoon market moved from decline to sharpness, with a prominent upward trend, eventually standing above 732 taels. Those who had not settled their June contracts found that the premium was only 2 taels, still offered by short sellers. The overall situation of the day is recorded below:

Morning Session Immediately Reveals Peak

The opening price for July contracts in the morning session rose sharply by 12 taels and 8 mace, reaching 732 taels. The previous day, major banks and American banks each fell by one-eighth, and private cables were also slightly down. The market appeared weak, but buyers were active, with Yuan Mao Yong, Hong Kang Yong, and Wupin, etc., all entering the market, reaching 33.5 taels. At that time, Da De Cheng, Wan Xing, Rui Xing, Shun Li, Tong Tai Chang, Zhi Feng Yong, Yi Feng Yong, Ding Chang, etc., all sold, causing the price to plummet by 5 taels. Furthermore, with offers coming from Mumbai, August US dollars were priced at 30.8125 yuan, and September required 31 yuan to sell. English gold for August was priced at 1 shilling and 8 pence. Consequently, at 9:15 AM, the price was 728 taels and 7 mace. After 5-6 minutes, it rose by 3 taels, then quickly retreated by over 2 taels. This was due to varying payouts from different firms. At 9:30 AM, the shilling opening price narrowed by 0.125, and the US dollar by 0.375. Subsequently, Tong Tai Chang, Da Xing Yong, etc., entered the market, immediately raising the price by 3 taels. At 9:40 AM, it reached 732 taels and 3 mace. Afterwards, the US dollar seemed firmer, with September contracts trading at 31.125 yuan. There were also many sellers in the market, including Fu Chang, Da De Cheng, Yu He, and Wan Xing. Near 10:00 AM, it was 728 taels and 8 mace. Shortly after, Qian Chang Xiang, Hong Kang Yong, Ri Chang, Zhi Feng Yong, etc., bought in, reaching 730 taels and 8 mace. At 10:15 AM, it began to decline again as Yuan Mao Yong, Yi Feng Yong, Yuan Tai, Fu Tai Heng, and the Dalian gang, etc., sold extensively. The Japanese Commercial Bank also sold July US dollars at 30.6875 yuan, and Anda offered June at 30.5 yuan. Until after 11:20 AM, it was 728 taels and 1 mace. However, within an hour, the price fluctuated by just over 1 tael, then quickly returned by over 1 tael. Da De Cheng re-entered the market, and Heng Chang Yong, etc., also purchased, reaching 729.5 taels at 11:30 AM. The market then closed at 729.1 taels, with Wupin trading at a premium of 0.6 mace. The indicative price was changed to 0.03 taels, with an estimated 74-75 taels pressed down.

Afternoon Market: From Decline to Sharpness Again

The afternoon market opened at 729 taels, then 728 taels and 3 mace, followed by 729 taels and 4 mace, but trading was limited. After 2:30 PM, Tong Tai Chang, the Dalian gang, Yuan Da Yong, etc., sold, and the US dollar appeared weak. Shanghai offered August at 30.8125 to 30.9375 yuan, and English gold for September could settle at 1 shilling, 8 pence, and 0.125. At 2:45 PM, it was 728 taels. Afterwards, it rebounded, driven by interbank trading of June English gold at 1 shilling, 7 pence, and 0.9375, and June US dollars at 30.4375 yuan, with August contracts trading at 30.8125 yuan. Additionally, Fu Xing Yong, Yuan Mao Yong, Wan Xing, etc., bought in, propelling the price upwards by 5 taels, reaching 733 taels at 4:10 PM. During this time, fluctuations were no more than a few cash or at most a little over 1 tael. It then retreated slightly by 1 tael and 2 mace, to 731 taels and 8 mace. By the 4:30 PM closing bell, the price was 732 taels and 3 mace, an increase of 13 taels and 1 mace compared to last Saturday. Wupin traded at a premium of 0.7 mace. The maximum price for the day was 733.5 taels, and the minimum was 728 taels, a difference of 5.5 taels. The indicative price was estimated at 74-70 taels pressed down. Accounts showed 32 taels for June and 29 taels for July, with a supplementary water charge of 32 taels in the afternoon and 35 taels. The naked strip added 9.75 taels.

On the trading floor, statistics showed that Qian Chang Xiang, Yuan Kang Xiang, Heng Xing Yuan, Yuan Da Yong, and Hong Kang Yong all bought in. Tong Tai Chang, Shun Li, Yuan Mao Yong, Da De Cheng, Fu Tai Heng, Yi Feng Yong, Yuan Tai, Fu Xing Yong, and Xie Xing Yong all sold. Wan Xing, Zhi Feng Yong, Yu He, etc., had mixed buying and selling. Last Week's American Cotton

In Irregular Fluctuations

But the New Cotton Crop is Progressing Well

New York, May 20, telegram reporting on the cotton market situation for the week: This week's raw cotton market situation fluctuated. Industry purchases and short-covering at price drops were enough to create a stable sentiment. The lack of rapid progress in Congress to balance the US budget and the unsatisfactory actions in the securities market caused some people to sell in disappointment. However, there was no selling pressure in the South, and the prices were already very low. Therefore, when the market price continued to fall, a buying trend emerged. There was no active action from both buyers and sellers, which shows that people in the market want to wait for the actions of Washington officials and the development of cotton crops and business conditions. In the past week, cotton crops have developed more slowly due to low humidity and overcast skies in the southwest and dry soil in the southeast. However, the slow progress of cotton crops did not affect the market sentiment. As for the increase or decrease in cotton fields, the general opinion has not changed. Most people in the cotton industry believe that the cotton crop has started well. Japan's demand in the South has already decreased, and there are not many sales in the interior. The base price is still stable.

Silk and Tea: Fresh Silkworm Cocoon Price in Xinchang is Low, Self-drying

The Highest Price for Foreign Varieties is Only 30 Yuan

The amount of spring silkworms raised in various cities and villages in Xinchang has been greatly reduced. In addition, the weather has been bad, with alternating cold and heat, and excessive rainfall. Silkworm diseases are rampant, and many are discarded. The cocoon production has been reduced and only accounts for less than 30% of the usual harvest. Only two or three cocoon brokers in the entire county have opened scales, and they all restrict the cocoon price, specializing in improved varieties of cocoons. The highest price is only 30 yuan, and the local varieties are only 24-25 yuan. However, farmers need about 50 yuan for silkworm capital, so the losses are too great. Most of them are carrying them back to dry them using local methods, and the cocoon market is almost lifeless.

Overseas Silk Telegrams Not Relayed

Yesterday, the silk market of foreign firms in this port was still quiet. The raw silk telegrams sent to overseas European and American firms last week were not relayed to Shanghai yesterday morning. Both Chinese and foreign silk merchants were watching and not moving forward, and the market was quiet with no transactions.

Free Talk

The Sayings of Ma Xiangbo, the Ninety-Three-Year-Old

Cai Yuanpei Reads Latin

— Lai

When I was young, it was very difficult to read foreign books. There were no dictionaries or grammar books. I translated the French grammar book, and I compiled the lecture notes for Latin for Aurora University.

At that time, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Jusheng, and Wang Kangnian all insisted on studying Latin. I advised them to study English and French, which were more practical. They refused, saying that Latin was the source of Western writing and must be studied. So I had to agree. Later, I taught them Cicero's works. The enthusiasm of young people like Cai, Zhang, and Wang for learning was truly admirable! I still remember Cai Yuanpei teaching at Nanyang Public School in Xujiahui. I lived in a building in front of Tushanwan. Every morning, Yuanpei would walk from Nanyang Public School, about four or five li, to study Latin with me. Sometimes, at five o'clock, when it was still dark, Yuanpei would shout softly outside: "Xiangbo! Xiangbo!" I was very surprised that someone was coming to see me so early in the morning. I opened the window and looked down, and it was Cai Yuanpei. I quickly waved my hand and said to him: "It's too early, it's too early. Come back at eight or nine o'clock!" Cai Yuanpei, that good child, had to leave disappointed.

Summer Parrots at Shichahai

—

| Miscellaneous Writings on the Old Capital - 5 |

The intense sunlight shines directly onto the ground without any obstruction. The willows droop their heads, breathing subtly. People are steamed with a little sweat by this scorching atmosphere, lazily afraid to move. From the top of some tree comes a burst of cicada sounds, as if to say that high summer has arrived.

After lunch, it is almost the hottest time, especially in this desert-like old city. All the moisture in the soil is being evaporated. If you don't find a cool place to spend this long day, then you may be annoyed by the weather.

Around one o'clock, E and I couldn't stand sitting in the study. We didn't have the usual interest in turning over posts and reading inscriptions. Finally, braving the scorching sun, we strolled across the lonely long street until we reached Shichahai. There was only bright sunlight lying on the road, and not even the sound of a camel bell could be heard.

When we arrived at Shichahai, it had already been arranged like a summer resort. Many thatched huts were built continuously along the wide, lotus-filled water. However, all sides were open, so that one could avoid the sun and feel the gentle breeze. This was indeed a suitable place to spend this long day. E and I made a pot of tea and chose a quieter place to sit down. After sitting for a while, we felt a little cooler, so we wanted to move around again. The edge of Shichahai was lined with connected cool sheds and stall canopies, forming a long street. The long street was full of tourists. The so-called Northern-style women with bound feet, wearing brightly colored clothes, were like butterflies, showing off their flower-like姿态 in the crowd, and their lively eyes would occasionally glance at you from under their sparse hair. Or they would decorate this barren Shichahai into a charming palace with a gilded small fan, as if this high summer had returned to the spring day of flowers and birds. When I was stranded on the journey in the sweltering summer every year, I couldn't help but think of this fascinating Shichahai.

World Short News

— Haike

Heat-Conducting Wallpaper: England has recently invented a heat-conducting wallpaper. When pasted on the walls, it can generate mild heat in the room. It has been successfully tested several times. The Canadian Pacific Railway Company's regular mail steamer, "Duchess of Richmond," has this wallpaper pasted on the ceilings of several cabins. Even in extremely cold weather, the room feels like spring. The origin of this invention comes from a special type of clothing worn by aviators. When flying in cold weather or to extremely high altitudes, they have to wear this heat-conducting clothing. The method is to weave thin radio copper wires into the fabric like a net. When an electric current is passed through, it can conduct heat without feeling cold. The invention of heat-conducting wallpaper is essentially the same. The paper material used is isolated and non-combustible. Thin electric wires are passed behind the paper, but they are not visible on the surface, looking like ordinary wallpaper. When the current is turned on, the walls will generate mild warmth.

Humorous Instruction

— Fei Wenbao

In modern wedding ceremonies, it is necessary to invite a venerable and virtuous marriage officiant. This is an indispensable character.

Yingchuan student Tong Hongnong and Ms. Hongnong were married during the national crisis. As usual, they invited a famous person to officiate the wedding. After reading the marriage certificate, the officiant, as usual, delivered a few words of instruction. In addition to two auspicious platitudes, he added three very witty humorous instructions to the bride, which were:

"At critical moments, you must bear the pain and not resist."

At the time, the bride seemed to want to laugh but couldn't after hearing these words. I don't know if she was shy or annoyed.

Two Nineteens in the North and South

— Shi Yan Ye

The soldiers defending our country in the Battle of Shanghai are the Nineteenth Route Army. With an army of 30,000, they faced an enemy four times their size. With flesh and blood, they faced sharp weapons. They fought fiercely for a month, repeatedly defeating the enemy. The loyalty, courage, and heroism of the Nineteenth Army are praised not only by our countrymen but also respected by people all over the world. Now, the humiliating armistice agreement has been signed. Damn the Japanese! They considered Shanghai unworthy of attention and abandoned the south for the north, concentrating their efforts to seize our eastern provinces. Looking north to the sky, the situation at Shanhaiguan is extremely urgent. The defending general there is He Zhuguo. The troops under He's command are the Nineteenth Brigade. The people of the South have already seen how the Southern Nineteen, with their spirit of sacrifice, inflicted great wounds on the enemy, won national glory, and enhanced international standing. It is a pity that they were hindered by treacherous officials and could not achieve complete success. Therefore, we can only hope that the Northern Nineteen will continue the fight to kill the enemy. According to reports, the Japanese troops demanded the right to freely suppress bandits in the area within eighty li of Yuguan. Brigade Commander He told them, "The bandits within Chinese territory will be suppressed by the Chinese army. We do not need others to do it for us. I, the brigade commander, am different from others. If anyone endangers the people within my jurisdiction, I will fight them with all my strength. I am not afraid of being crushed to pieces." A few words, full of righteousness and awe. We firmly believe that the Northern Nineteen can also resist Japan without a doubt. One soldier guarding the pass will not allow the barbarian cavalry to invade. A single pillar supporting the great mansion, worthy of being a cornerstone of the country. Moreover, we will drive the enemy out of the border, paving the way for the recovery of lost territory, and unite the righteous army to drive the invaders from the three islands. We will see loyalty, courage, and heroism, and the Southern Nineteen will not be able to claim all the credit. However, the atmosphere in the Northeast is filled with non-resistance, and the Northern Nineteen is only a single brigade. With the weakness of a single brigade, trapped in a harsh environment, their hardships are much greater than those of the Southern Nineteen. We hope that General He can uphold the spirit of being crushed to pieces and vow to shed the last drop of blood at Shanhaiguan. Then, hardships will not be a concern, and the enemy will not be difficult to defeat. Therefore, this same Nineteenth, whether the Southern one is strong or the Northern one is strong, we dare not say for sure.

A Visit with Mrs. Gandhi (Part 1)

— Huang Yingdai

She is an Unknown Woman

India has been conquered by England for a long time, but Gandhi's non-violent resistance has made him admired by the people of the world. We already know about Gandhi's knowledge and personality, but we probably don't know everything about Mrs. Gandhi. Because she is an unknown woman, "The Woman that nobody knows." This time, she was imprisoned for forty-five days. After being released, H.J. Greenwall, a news reporter for the Daily News, visited Mrs. Gandhi. Now, in order to help readers understand this unknown woman, I will translate the interview with Mrs. Gandhi that Greenwall published after the visit:

I have visited this unknown woman, and she is Mrs. Gandhi. She has just been released from prison after serving her first 45-day sentence.

It was indeed a difficult task. We waited for three consecutive days for the visit because she happened to be participating in a conference. Later, she finally walked into the room where we were waiting. The room had a flat roof. From the opening, we could see the foothills of Malabar Hill. The Indian temple was just opposite the room.

"How did you feel in prison?" This was the first question I asked her. Mrs. Gandhi is a very short woman. Her height is probably less than four feet. After smoothing out her black-edged clothes, she replied:

"Not very good; indeed," she said with a smile, "because I am Gandhi's wife, they treat me differently. Among the prisoners, I am the"

"Considered the most favored."

Our seats were very close to the stars, and the sky was quickly darkening. Mrs. Gandhi didn't say much, and none of it was in English, so our conversation was entirely translated.

The number of people in the room quickly increased. The first to appear was a young woman wearing glasses. She interrupted our conversation with her experiences of six months in prison. Later, a young girl came to tell Mrs. Gandhi how she and four companions were being interfered with by the police's freedom. Finally, a young man wearing glasses entered my left ear. He loudly exclaimed how brutal the people on the northwest border were behaving.

Mrs. Gandhi was barefoot, wearing a pair of glass bangles on each of her thin arms.

I know that she is 55 years old, but judging from her sparse gray hair, by European standards, she is at least over 60 years old.

Mrs. Gandhi now has many young prison companions, who are all guilty of underpaying the salt tax. According to Mrs. Gandhi, these young women were thrown on the ground by the police, their clothes were torn, and they were abused very painfully.

Finger Sacrifice for Burial

— Rui Yucheng

A resident of our county, Mr. Chen, graduated from Nanjing Higher Normal School. He has served as a Chinese language teacher in various secondary schools. He is currently the director of the county's Public Education Center. He is a man of deep emotions, especially devoted to his spouse. Several years ago, he married Ms. Mao from the same hometown. The family was very harmonious. Two years later, Ms. Mao became pregnant. Mr. Chen was secretly delighted because this was the crystallization of their love. Unexpectedly, after a few months, Ms. Mao suddenly had a miscarriage and, feeling heartbroken, fell ill. Mr. Chen took care of her day and night, without any fatigue. On one hand, he hired famous doctors to diagnose and treat her. He personally decocted the medicine, not relying on servants, for fear of making mistakes. Who knew that Ms. Mao's illness would gradually become more severe, leaving the doctors helpless. Mr. Chen felt distressed, but on the surface, he remained calm and served her. After seven days, Ms. Mao passed away. At the time of her death, she held Mr. Chen's left hand tightly. She could no longer speak, but her hand remained tightly clasped until her last breath. The family wanted to pry it open, but Mr. Chen insisted not to. He told people to bring a sharp knife and cut off the four fingers of his left hand, so that his beloved deceased wife could hold them. She held them all the way to the coffin and into the earth.

This story has spread almost throughout the hometown. Mr. Chen is still alive today. People call him "Mr. One Finger."

Records of Military Horses in the Double Pavilion (61)

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Eight: Boundless Sorrow and Repentance, Difficult to Achieve Open-Mindedness; Extreme Singing and Dancing, to Witness Authority

After hearing these gentle and sad words, Liang Xiaoyun glanced at An Yutian unintentionally. Seeing him bowing his head to his chest, his heart seemed to be filled with infinite sorrow and shame. She couldn't help but sigh deeply and said, "In that case, I am not as open-minded as others. But I have my own difficulties and had no choice but to do this. Now that things have reached this point, I can only betray others. When I have the opportunity in the future, I will explain my feelings to him." After saying this, she took out the check, folded it into a small square, and clipped it between her slender fingers. Then, she lightly tore it apart into two pieces, then four pieces from the two, and then eight pieces from the four, until there were countless pieces. With a wave of her hand, these many pieces of paper flew like butterflies, fluttering and falling onto the soft carpet in the room without making a sound. As a result, the three people in the room all felt an inexplicable sadness, which attacked their hearts coldly. They looked at each other and froze in that humorous realm. Wei Zhuomou couldn't bear the silence and quietly wanted to escape. An Yutian made small talk and wanted to get up to see him off, but Wei Zhuomou turned his head and made a funny face at him. He also raised his right hand and touched his thumb and index finger together, making a slight strange sound. He slumped back down and let him go on his own. After another moment of silence, Liang Xiaoyun slowly wiped the moist marks around her eyes with her small handkerchief and gave An Yutian an extremely unnatural bitter smile. "Let's not think about this guilty thing anymore. Let me tell you a little about how I handled your first business today. Nowadays, the best way to maneuver in the official arena is to go through the inner line. Although Fifth Madam Ye and I are quite close, and that path can be considered the right one to take, it is still not enough to rely on selling empty favors. So-called worldly ways and human sentiments still require a considerable gift to be used as a stepping stone. I was fortunate to remember when I lived with her in the same troupe, I had a customer who gave me a very large chicken-heart-shaped jadeite ring. The color was dripping green, with no flaws at all. Although the price was not high, only a few thousand yuan, it would be very difficult to find the same one again. When she saw it at the time, she was very fond of it and praised it highly. At that time, I couldn't give it to her for no reason. It just happened to be saved for today and came in handy as a gift. It is difficult to give her other things that would suit her. It is also inconvenient to show too many traces. So, I just sent this one up, and it was very suitable."

Supplement to the Local Edition of the Shen Bao

Sayings

Free City

— Buddha

The sound of a free city has been spreading for a long time, but I believe that there is no possibility of it being realized when viewed through common sense or human reason.

However, yesterday I heard a very peculiar conversation from a certain important person in a certain organization. He said,

During this Shanghai incident, our people suffered heavy losses, and we must find a way to help them. We are now planning to build two main roads in Shanghai, one from the southernmost point to the northernmost point, and one from the easternmost point to the westernmost point. We are also planning to build a residential area in a certain location to make it easier for people to solve the problem of housing. The estimated construction cost is about 10 million yuan. If that is not enough, we will add another 5 million yuan.

Readers, please close your eyes and think about this. What a grand and ambitious plan!

Ordinary residents will naturally welcome it when they hear that there are cheap houses available. Landlords and land brokers will see an opportunity to make money and will naturally not object. Even residents living closer to the concessions will consider this a one-time solution because they have suffered losses from moving their establishments due to repeated wartime events.

Alas! What else can I say?

Science

Chemical Arts and Small Industry

— Nai Zheng

We see glass with engraved text and picture designs that are very beautiful. These are mostly Japanese goods. They don't use knives to engrave them because glass is very hard and difficult to cut. They use chemical methods to engrave, the procedure is simple, and the cost of the chemicals used is very cheap. It's a pity that our country doesn't have this kind of small industry yet, mainly because not many people know about it. So, I'm introducing it now to promote it.

(1) Simple Engraving Method

First, coat the glass pane with beeswax. Use a small knife or needle to carve away the wax, writing words or drawing pictures. Then, take a large-mouthed lead bottle (made of light lead; other types of containers are unusable, or they will melt and crack). Inside, put fifteen parts calcium fluoride and nineteen parts sulfuric acid. Place it on a tripod iron stand and heat it with an alcohol lamp. Then, you can take the carved glass pane and place it over the mouth of the lead bottle to be fumed. At the same time, cover the back of the glass pane with a cold, wet cloth to prevent the wax from melting. After seven or eight minutes, silver-white will appear on the glass lines where there is no wax. Then, take it down, scrape off the wax with a knife, and wash it in hot water. The text or picture design will appear. The depth of the engraving is directly proportional to the fuming time.

(2) Fine Engraving Method

Take calcium fluoride and sulfuric acid (same amounts as in the previous method) and put them in a light lead retort. Seal the mouth of the bottle with a rubber stopper with a hole. Then, take an empty lead bottle and also seal the mouth tightly with a rubber stopper with a hole. Then, insert the two ends of a rubber tube into the two rubber stopper holes to connect the two bottles. Then, place the empty lead bottle in an ice bucket (add salt to the ice). Then, place the retort on an alcohol lamp and heat it. The two substances inside will melt and turn into gas, which will pass through the rubber tube to the empty bottle, where it will condense into liquid. Wait until all the gas has turned into liquid, then seal it with a non-porous rubber stopper and place it in a cool, damp place. Then, take a glass pane and coat it with wax and carve a design as in the previous method. Dip a rubber brush (shaped like a pencil) into this liquid and apply it to the glass where the wax has been removed. After half an hour, wash it off with warm water. The pattern made with this method is clearer and finer than the previous method, but the procedure is a little more cumbersome.

Also, the stripes and grids on the outside of measuring cups are made using the above method. If you want to make frosted glass (used in cameras), you can coat one side of the glass pane with beeswax, immerse it in the prepared liquid, quickly take it out with bamboo chopsticks (never use your hands), and rinse it in clean water.

Regarding the method of engraving calligraphy and paintings on glass, an article was published last month, but it was slightly different from the method in this article and did not include a fine engraving method, so I am re-recording it.

He Haoyi

Embarrassed

— Li Chu

One afternoon of a week, I went into the ×× bookstore to select and buy a few practical books. It happened to be this Sunday, and there were particularly many customers, especially in this bookstore which had several modern female clerks. These customers, flowing in an endless stream, seemed to be visiting because of the presence of the female clerks. People in business are truly good at adapting to the psychology of customers. In this era of open social interaction, the boundaries between men and women have long been broken. Why not take this opportunity? On the one hand, it can expand business, and on the other hand, it can help women's productivity. It is a win-win situation and worth doing.

I stepped into the store and saw that there were also people who genuinely wanted to buy books, and there were also those who were looking around without buying. The male and female clerks didn't seem particularly busy either. Beside one of the counters stood a female customer, around twenty years old. Inside the counter were two female clerks, not much different in age from her. The female customer had been looking for a long time before she finally found a romance novel she wanted to read, and then asked one of the female clerks in a gentle tone, "What's this book like for romance matters?" The tall and slender female clerk smiled but didn't answer, while the other, plump female clerk抢着said, "Very good! Very good! You can buy one for reference!" Little did she know that it would infuriate the female clerk who had smiled and didn't answer earlier, who shouted loudly, "Ah! You've read it, you know, you're someone with experience in love!" As soon as she said this, the general public in the store turned to look at them and laugh. There were also a few who hadn't heard clearly who were saying in low voices, "What's going on? Could they be love rivals jealous of each other?" Seeing that everyone's expressions were paying attention to them, they felt very ashamed. Their goose-egg-colored faces, tinged with peach red, suddenly flushed red to their ears, revealing a very embarrassed look.

A Dream

A Glimpse Inside Yuqing Palace

— Youqi

Ah! This is Yuqing Palace, as I just stepped inside, I discovered that it was clearly marked above the round hole.

In front of the dignified statue of the god, tall candle stands and incense tripods are erected. Their tops and insides are adorned with dots of fiery red and handfuls of incense sticks. The smoke from the candles and incense combines and rises gently. Due to the baptism of fire and smoke, the statue of the god, who enjoys the offerings, has lost its original color. At the same time, everything else in the hall enjoys the same treatment, blessed by the blessings of fortune.

"Would you like to order some incense and candles?" The incense and candle vendor in the hall constantly uses his amiable tone and smiling face to ask the men and women who come and go, especially the old women.

"Five bundles of incense, five pairs of candles," the believers hanging yellow cloth bags buy very generously. They worship, pray silently, and scatter the burning incense in their hands among the tripods of the gods. Furthermore, they uniformly allow the other side halls to enjoy the same treatment.

"Clatter, clatter," copper coins naturally fly from their hands into the round bamboo tube that stands beside the Buddha's table, having been soaked in incense for a long time.

"Kind ladies, may you be prosperous..." A well-trained beggar also squeezes in, begging behind these believers, hoping to gain some comforting ideal.

"Go away, nothing there,"

"Ah! Compassionate...doesn't care about this..." He continues to follow and plead.

"That is the Buddha! You..." Very lightly and naturally, it flows from the mouth of the middle-aged believer who had previously bought incense and is now stepping towards another hall.

Ah! He is probably sighing that he himself has not become a Buddha and cannot aspire to this sincere offering, right? Her figure is lost in the smoke, and he still gazes into the misty smoke.

Bin Wei

A Pitiful Rickshaw Puller

— Xi

"I've been out for half a day today, and haven't earned a single cent. What will I eat when I go back?" A rickshaw puller, about forty years old, pulling a heavy rickshaw, walked slowly on the road, saying this to himself in frustration.

Just then, a well-dressed gentleman in a suit walked out from across the street. The rickshaw puller thought to himself, my savior has arrived, and quickly pulled the rickshaw to greet him.

"Sir! Where to? I'll pull you there!" the rickshaw puller asked this, hoping that the well-dressed gentleman would get into his rickshaw immediately.

"How much to the Tianchan Theatre?" the well-dressed gentleman asked. "I'll take you there! Thirty cents will do," the rickshaw puller replied.

"Twenty cents, will you go?" the well-dressed gentleman asked.

"Make it easy, give me twenty-three cents," the rickshaw puller replied.

"Not one more, if you don't go, forget it," the well-dressed gentleman said, and walked forward.

"What is one more cent to you?" the rickshaw puller pleaded.

The well-dressed gentleman ignored him and strode forward.

"Such a well-off gentleman, not willing to pay even three more cents, really is..." the rickshaw puller said to himself.

"Sir! Wait, I'll pull you for twenty cents," because he thought that he hadn't earned a single cent today, so he called out to the well-dressed gentleman and pulled the rickshaw to follow him. Just as he arrived, another rickshaw came from across the street.

"Tianchan Theatre, twenty cents, will you go?" the well-dressed gentleman asked that rickshaw puller.

"I'll take you!" that rickshaw puller replied.

"Sir, I was the one who agreed with you first," this rickshaw puller said, looking at the well-dressed gentleman.

"Aren't you going?" the well-dressed gentleman said angrily. He sat in that rickshaw, and that rickshaw puller pulled it away as if flying. This rickshaw puller watched the rickshaw disappear, then put down his rickshaw, lowered his head, and remained silent. After a while, his eyes turned red, and hot tears flowed out.

Nonsense

The Effect of "Looking at Incense Heads"

Warning the Foolish

Since the neighbor Mrs. Li's health deteriorated, her daughter "Rong" has been as anxious as an ant on a hot pot, spinning around in circles.

"Hey! Miss! I think you should ask the 'Incense Head Reader' 'Double Immortal' to come and look at the incense head, it's very interesting!" This was the Zhang family's maid Hu Ma, suggesting to "Rong."

"What do you mean by 'Double Immortal'? What exactly is 'Looking at Incense Heads'?" "Rong" asked her, full of surprise and curiosity.

"Well! 'Looking at Incense Heads' is one of the 'Double Immortal's' businesses. 'Double Immortals' are people who are born with two pupils in their eyes, so they can see everything in the underworld. Just light incense and candles, pray sincerely, and focus on the incense head, the images of gods, demons, ghosts, and monsters will appear completely, and thus judge people's fortunes and misfortunes. This is the most accurate. Now the × Immortal in × place is also a 'Double Immortal.' Its 'Looking at Incense Heads' is extraordinarily effective and famous far and wide. Why not invite them to try it out?" She explained the effectiveness of the "Double Immortal" and the benefits of "Looking at Incense Heads" in detail, praised the abilities of × Immortal, and strongly recommended it.

"Ah! Really? That's great. I'm so anxious that I don't know what to do, you go and invite them for me!" "Rong" was overjoyed and couldn't wait to call her to do it immediately. The next afternoon, × Immortal came as promised. All the arrangements for burning incense and lighting candles were complete, and "Rong" was also reverent and respectful, kneeling and praying, "Your family's ancestors have a wronged ghost who is entangled here. You must ask a 'Taoist priest' to capture them. In addition, you have offended the 'Fengdu Emperor,' the 'Northern Yin Funeral Department,' and the 'Teng Snake' and 'Five Saints'... all the gods. You must set up grand sacrifices and pray with great etiquette. At least you must thank the Bodhisattva with thirty-six tables. If you do this, I guarantee that the patient will immediately turn the corner and get well in three days." × Immortal, based on observations from the incense head, gave instructions one by one, and "Rong" followed them respectfully as if obeying an imperial edict.

In the evening, "Taoist priests" and "Taibao" 丨 These types are prevalent in the Punan area, specializing in thanking the Bodhisattva, 丨 came one after another, performing their work of "doing rituals" and "thanking the Bodhisattva." Therefore, gongs and drums shook the sky, and the Li residence was extraordinarily lively, and the expenses were also considerable.

When the "Taoist priests" and "Taibao" finished their work and left the scene, the old lady also passed away with a sigh, dying peacefully in her sleep.
